Rectification is not easy, but if they are allowed to fight each other, they will all perish. How can this be the blessing of the national economy and the people's livelihood? Therefore, this guild hall will not avoid difficulties and will earnestly rectify. The three major guidelines previously agreed upon have been unanimously signed by the retail industry, which shows that industry colleagues have a deep understanding. This guild hall is now submitting the aforementioned guidelines to the competent authorities for record in accordance with industry regulations, hoping that industry colleagues can abide by them consistently. If there are still those who comply in appearance but disobey in reality, regardless of whether they are members or non-members, they will be reported to the Social Affairs Bureau for punishment in accordance with Article 26 of the industry regulations. There will be no favoritism. The day before yesterday, 38 industry colleagues jointly sent a letter to me, pointing out that a certain silk and satin bureau did not comply with the guidelines. This guild hall immediately sent a letter to correct it. The silk and satin bureau has accepted the advice, and others who have not complied have also been corrected by sending letters. In summary, this guild hall has an unshirkable duty to revive national silk, but it is hoped that all industry colleagues will work together. If there are opinions to be stated, you can feel free to do so and do not need to issue anonymous letters. As for organizing a national silk exhibition, the purpose is to promote the advantages of national silk and enable all sectors to have a correct understanding of it. In the future, we will also need the help of the press.

Criminal Lawsuit Filed with the Court

Requesting Assistance from Fellow Association Yesterday

Association Sends Letter to Water Patrol Team to Stop

From Floating Buoy No. 17 to Floating Buoy No. 30 in Yangshupu, Shanghai, the mooring and unmooring of all vessels of various shipping companies berthing or departing at that location has been contracted by a Ningbo man named Chen Shenbao since 1926. The shipping companies subsidize Chen Shenbao's labor costs of five or six yuan each month. The total monthly income is also around one hundred yuan. Therefore, Chen has been running this business for nine years, working hard and saving carefully, and now he is well-off. However, Chen Shenbao's experience is well known to his colleagues at the pier, who are very envious. There is no shortage of those who want

to replace him. Unexpectedly, the other day, Shen Youcai, a local who is engaged in loading and unloading work at the pier, gathered more than 30 accomplices and, in three rowing boats, propped up to Chen's work place in Yangshupu, driving away Chen and Chen's assistants, and replacing them in the mooring and unmooring work for various shipping vessels from Floating Buoy No. 17 to Floating Buoy No. 30. At that time, Chen refused to accept it and also led his assistants

to fight back, but eventually retreated due to being overwhelmed. However, he could not bear to give up the business rights that had been in place for many years. Therefore, in addition to entrusting lawyer Liu Shiqi to file a criminal lawsuit with the local court, he went to the Ningbo Fellow Association in Shanghai on Tibet Road the day before yesterday evening to request assistance. Based on the above-mentioned facts, the association specially sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau Water Patrol Team yesterday morning,

requesting strict prohibition. The original letter is recorded below. Before the matter is resolved by the court, we request that Your Captain strictly prohibit it and issue a notice to avoid disputes. We hereby send this letter to you, hoping that you will investigate and handle it accordingly. This letter is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau Water Patrol Team.

Robbery at Yucheng Silver Company on Henan Road 128

Company Employees First Bound Up

Eight Thousand Four Hundred Yuan Stolen

As winter approaches and the weather turns colder, a class of petty thieves, mostly driven by hunger and cold, resort to desperate measures. As a result, robbery cases have been occurring frequently for the past month, reaching alarming numbers. However, a careful examination of these individuals' actions suggests they are premeditated and deeply familiar with the inner workings. Otherwise, they could never be so agile. Since the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank was robbed of over four thousand yuan the day before yesterday, all parties are in pursuit. Unexpectedly, the Yucheng Silver Company on Henan Road was reported to have been robbed yesterday morning. It is learned that the company is located at No. 111, 2nd Floor, Jinxing Building, No. 505 Henan Road, Public Concession. The manager is Xie Xuchu from Shaoxing. Yesterday morning, around 9:00 AM, the company sent employees to withdraw over eight thousand yuan in bank notes from the China Industrial Bank. They immediately locked it in the safe. Before the key was even fully turned, three robbers, each wearing a long robe and brandishing a pistol from their sleeves, broke into the company's office. They threatened the staff to remain silent, then proceeded to bind all those in the office and confine them to a single room, guarded by one of the robbers. They then interrogated who was in charge of accounting and demanded the safe keys, making off with all eight thousand four hundred and eighty-odd yuan in bank notes that had just been stored. The robbers then hastily fled downstairs. By the time the staff managed to break free of their bonds and chase them downstairs, the robbers had long disappeared without a trace. They immediately reported the incident to Manager Xie Xuchu, who in turn reported it to the police station, requesting an investigation. Upon receiving the report, the police immediately dispatched detectives to investigate the scene and inquire about the appearance and features of the robbers to aid in the pursuit. However, it is noteworthy that the robbers were well-informed, agile in their methods, and always successful, especially focusing on financial institutions, which is worthy of further investigation.

Forgery of School Certificate Case Appealed and Returned for Retrial 129

Zhang Zhen, from Baoshan, studied at the private Qunzhi University on Caobadu Roberts Road. The school closed down in 1930. Zhang Zhen then forged a graduation certificate from the school to defraud others and petitioned the Ministry of Judicial Administration for qualification, obtaining a lawyer's certificate. The Ministry of Judicial Administration detected suspicious circumstances and transferred the case to the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate for investigation. A newly carved wooden seal of "(Shanghai Private Qunzhi University) (Fengtian Fengcheng Yucai) (Fujian Pucheng Puguan) Two Middle Schools" and private seals of Zhang Xiangwen and others, totaling fifteen, were found at Zhang's residence, along with blank graduation certificates, etc. Zhang Zhen was immediately detained, interrogated, and prosecuted in the criminal court. Zhang Zhen was sentenced to eight months of imprisonment and a fine of four hundred yuan for forging seals. Zhang Zhen refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the original court. As a result, the appeal was rejected. Zhang then appealed to the Jiangsu High Court, and the High Court issued a verdict: (Main text) The original judgment is revoked, and the case is returned to the Shanghai Local Court for a new trial. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Guan Liting specially opened the Tenth Court for the trial. Zhang Zhen hired lawyer Wang Peiyuan to appear in court to defend him. After the judge took his seat, he ordered the detained Zhang Zhen to be brought to the stand. Zhang stated that he was 24 years old, from Baoshan, residing at No. 9, Zhonghua Road, Ximen. He enrolled in Qunzhi University in the spring of 1927 and graduated in the summer of 1930, with over three hundred classmates. All the graduation certificates were entrusted to the defendant by Principal Luo Jie, who collected a handling fee of five yuan per certificate, totaling about thirty certificates, or over one hundred yuan. After obtaining the confession, the judge ordered him to be remanded in custody and to await a continued hearing at a later date.

Shooting Incident in a Brothel 130

Chen Xin Sentenced to Three Months Yesterday

Chen Xin, an employee of the Yifeng Sugar and Porcelain Factory, previously drank excessively at the Huanqiu Hong brothel. Later, he went to Lu Aiying, a prostitute at the Lihua brothel in Fuxiang Lane, Guangxi Road, and somehow took out his self-defense pistol and fired a shot, hitting Zhang Sujuan, a prostitute in the same courtyard, in the right leg. Chen was arrested by the police and prosecuted in the First Special Court under Article 282 of the Criminal Law. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Qian Hongye, the chief criminal judge of the First Special Court, continued the trial in Criminal Court No. 1. Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, stated that the injury to the victim, Zhang Sujuan, has been diagnosed by a doctor. The bullet hit the bone under the left leg, which is now fixed with a plaster cast and will take about four weeks to heal and should not result in a permanent disability. When questioned, Chen Xin confessed that it was indeed due to excessive drinking. The court informed him that Zhang Sujuan's mother had filed a civil suit, demanding compensation of six thousand yuan. What is your intention? He replied that he was unable to pay this amount. The court then ordered the commencement of arguments. After the police lawyer, Wang, made his argument, Chen's lawyer, Fan Gang, rose to respond, stating briefly that the charge of attempted murder brought by the police could not be sustained. At the time, the defendant was indeed confused by alcohol and his mind was unclear, and there was no intention to kill. However, negligence cannot be avoided. The defendant's family relies entirely on him for a living. The court should grant leniency and impose a particularly light sentence. Judge Qian then announced the verdict in court, sentencing Chen Xin to three months of imprisonment for using a method sufficient to cause death and injuring a person. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be offset at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. One pistol and five bullets were confiscated. The incidental civil suit was transferred to the civil court of this court for trial.

German Art Exhibition Scheduled to Open 131

Date: 4:00 PM on the 29th

Location: 9th Floor, YMCA, Baxianqiao

German Modern Art Products were exhibited at the German School in this city two years ago. At that time, due to the limited space and small scale, its excellent results have been deeply imprinted in the minds of Shanghai residents. Now, it is learned that there will be a large-scale exhibition again. The location has been selected on the 9th floor of the YMCA in Baxianqiao, Route Min Teh Ni Ying, French Concession, this city. It is scheduled to open at 4:00 PM on the 29th of this month, that is, this Thursday. The exhibition will be held there from 10:00 AM to 8:00 PM every day until the 5th of next month. The exhibits include a large number of oil paintings, watercolor paintings, copperplate paintings, pastel paintings, and woodcut art. Most of them are carefully crafted works by emerging German artists, depicting German city and rural landscapes. The prices are very low, ranging from two yuan to one hundred and twenty-five yuan, and most of the works are below twenty-five yuan, making them most suitable as Christmas gifts. The persons in charge are Mrs. Klippai, wife of the German Consul General in Shanghai, Mrs. Wang Rutang, wife of the former Minister of Foreign Affairs, Mrs. Lawrence, wife of the manager of the German firm Lihe Foreign Firm, and Ms. Huang, chairman of the Shanghai YWCA. It is heard that the admission ticket for this exhibition costs only five dimes, and all the proceeds from the ticket sales will be transferred to the Pudong Civilian Model Village to be used as a charitable act. Through this exhibition, the cultural relationship between China and Germany will be deepened.

Various Groups in Fuyang County Send Telegram to Shanghai Requesting Disaster Relief Due to Severe Drought 135

160,000 Disaster Victims Wandering the Roads

Hoping for Generous Relief Funds to Alleviate Suffering

Various groups such as the Fuyang County Party Department and the County Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to various charitable organizations in this city yesterday requesting disaster relief due to the severe disaster situation in the county. The original telegram stated: 'Respected recipients, Our Fuyang is located in the lower reaches of the Qiantang River. The areas along the river are all low-lying, while the surrounding villages are high-lying. Three days of rain will cause floods, turning the area into a swamp. Ten days of sunshine will cause rivers to dry up and fields to crack. Years of rice moth disasters and floods have followed one after another, like a sick man who has suffered from a long-term illness, whose vital energy and essence have been exhausted and who is confined to bed. But if the sick body has a chance to rest, then our people may have a chance to recover. Why is the heaven so unkind, sending down another terrible disaster? Since summer, it has been sunny and without rain, and the long drought has become a disaster. The rice seedlings have all withered. Early crops such as corn have had reduced harvests due to the lack of water. Autumn crops such as buckwheat have also withered one after another due to the early frost. In total, there are as many as 160,000 disaster victims in Fuyang. The cries of geese are everywhere, and refugees wander the roads. Prosperous families have become poor people, and the extremely poor have become starving people. They dig grass roots to fill their stomachs and peel tree bark to satisfy their hunger. In the blink of an eye, the weather will be cold and freezing, and the hungry people will have no clothes and no food. The tragic scene is unbearable to imagine. This is truly a great catastrophe in history and a great disaster in a century. Our association and others serve our hometown, with a strong sense of responsibility. Witnessing the tragic scene, it is difficult to sit idly by. In addition to exhausting our meager efforts to appeal to the local authorities in various counties for relief, we have always admired your association's concern for the suffering and your compassion for others. Relief does not distinguish between regions, and donations are made without regard to east or west. We dare to imitate the weeping of the prison gatekeeper to replace the call of Jiang Bo. We humbly hope that you will have compassion for the disaster victims, jointly seek rescue, and generously grant relief funds to alleviate their suffering. Either remit the funds to our association for distribution or send personnel to the disaster area for distribution. In any case, a steady stream of thousands of gold and ten thousand mirrors will arrive, and the survivors after the catastrophe will forever be grateful for the boundless merit. Urgent words, mixed with tears, kind clouds are in the hall, endlessly reluctant. Fuyang County Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang Zhejiang Province, County Farmers Association Relief Association, Women's Association, Committee for the Management of County Public Funds and Properties, County Chamber of Commerce, Stevedores' Union, etc., kowtow together.'"

Pudong Public Security Bureau Rectifies Traffic at Dongchang Wharf 136

Specifies Eleven Measures

Since the opening of the city ferry, the number of rickshaws at Dongchang Road Wharf in Pudong has increased significantly. Conflicts often arise due to soliciting business or arguing about fares. Zhang, the Director of the Pudong Public Security Bureau, gathered opinions from all parties to address this traffic issue and formulated eleven compromise measures, which were announced to passengers and rickshaw pullers for compliance. The measures are as follows: (1) There are 41 fixed rickshaws at Dongchang Road Wharf every day. The west end of the parking area is designated as the starting point. Latecomers or non-fixed rickshaws should line up neatly in order from east to west according to the prescribed sequence (one row if there are few cars, two rows if there are many cars). Rickshaw pullers are not allowed to leave their cars to solicit business at the wharf. (2) After fixed or non-fixed rickshaws transport passengers to the wharf, they must turn left and exit through the back door of Huatong Warehouse. They must not linger or solicit business directly, obstructing order and traffic. (3) Among the 41 fixed rickshaw pullers, one person should be drawn in rotation every day to be on duty (the rotation list will be determined separately) to maintain order in the wharf parking area. (4) The on-duty rickshaw puller's service hours are from 6:00 AM to 8:00 PM. (5) The on-duty rickshaw puller's meal expenses are borne by the non-on-duty fixed rickshaw pullers. Each person will pay a certain amount of copper coins to the on-duty rickshaw puller as meal expenses. (6) The on-duty rickshaw puller must wear a numbered uniform (style to be determined separately) during service hours for identification. (7) Starting from Dongchang Road Wharf, the minimum rickshaw fare is 15 copper coins. A full-day fare is $1.50, including meal expenses. Passengers can choose to tip for meal expenses. Thirteen hours is considered one day. The zero-hire fares to various places in Pudong are detailed in a separate table. A surcharge of 30 cents will be added for waiting over one hour, and so on. For those waiting for a long time, the fare can also be negotiated to some extent, but it should not exceed the all-inclusive price. (8) For pilgrims from Dongchang Road Wharf to Qinci Yangdian Temple, the round-trip fare is 60 cents. The round-trip fare to Qijia Temple is 80 cents. Even if the waiting time is longer, it must not be calculated according to the example of Article 7. (9) If passengers and rickshaw pullers know each other or have a special relationship and do not follow these measures, both parties are free to ride or pull. Others must not interfere with freedom on this pretext. (10) Those starting from Chunjiang Wharf can also refer to the compromise price list set by this sub-bureau. (11) These compromise measures will be implemented from the date of approval of the record.

Kidnapping Case Cracked in Zhenru 139

Three Kidnappers Captured on the Spot

Two Hostages Rescued in Suzhou

To Be Sent to Suzhou for Trial Within Days

Zhou Weilie, the director of the Second District of the Jiangsu River Police, has been planning the defense since his transfer, which is quite comprehensive. Unexpectedly, last month, Zhu Shouchun, the son of Jin Qiangui from Zhu Mazhuang, Hushu Pass, and Ni Mu, Bao and his son Yuan Yuan, grandson Xiao Laohu, etc. from Lushangwei Village in Wuxian County were kidnapped and ransomed successively. Afterwards, the district director immediately ordered the team to search and investigate in all directions. As a result, the case was solved in Zhenru the day before yesterday, and three kidnappers, Wang Ziqing, Guo Kuangsheng, and Liu Ziming, were captured on the spot, and two hostages were rescued. Two pistols were seized. The reporter of Huadong News Agency made a special investigation and recorded the following:

The Whole Family Was Kidnapped. On the evening of October 1st, at about 9:00 PM, more than ten robbers suddenly came to the home of Ni Mubao in Lushangwei Village, Wuxian County. They pried into the house from the roof of the wing room, then opened the gate and searched and robbed at will for about an hour. Before leaving, they kidnapped Ni Mubao and his son Yuan Yuan. On the night of October 3rd, several thieves came again and kidnapped his grandson Xiao Laohu for ransom. One of the kidnaped Ni Mubao has been rescued by the First Detachment of the Zhejiang Water Police at the Taihu Estuary, and several bandits have been arrested and sent to the Changxing County Government for trial. His son Yuan Yuan and grandson Xiao Laohu are still in the bandits' lair.

Letter Demanding Ransom. Jin Qiangui, a farmer in Zhu Mazhuang, Hushu Pass, is well-to-do. He has a son named Shouchun, who is seven years old. Qiangui and his wife love him very much. On the evening of the 18th of last month, at about 12:00 PM, they were suddenly robbed, and Shouchun was kidnapped. Afterwards, the whole family received three letters from the bandits, one stating that they lacked travel expenses, so they took this action, the second demanding 3,000 yuan to redeem the ticket, and the third asking Jin to personally bring the money to Zhenru Station in Shanghai by the 11:00 AM train the day before yesterday to redeem the ticket, explaining that after getting off the train, he should walk east along the motor road, and someone would come to contact him. The matter was detected by the detectives of the Second District of the River Police, who reported to the District Director Zhou Weilie. The director then ordered the detectives Ma Baisheng, Mao Wenlong, Shao Henglong, Wang Zhen, etc. to invite the client and give them the opportunity.

Three Bandits Arrested. The detectives first came to Shanghai to ask the Criminal Investigation Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Zhenru Public Security Sub-bureau for assistance. By about 3:00 PM, the time stipulated in the bandits' letter had arrived. The detectives disguised themselves and arranged the scene. Then, they instructed Jin to follow the indicated direction. About 300 meters away, one person in short clothes and two people in long gowns came forward to contact Jin. After about two minutes, the detectives drew their guns and surrounded the bandits. The bandits knew they had failed and ran away along the motor road towards Shanghai. The detectives also chased closely. The three bandits changed their plan and turned to the wasteland behind Jinan University to escape. Before they could take a dozen steps, a small river blocked them. In desperation, the bandits jumped into the river to escape. The police immediately dispersed on both sides of the river and captured the three bandits in one fell swoop.

Rescuing the Hostages. After the three bandits were arrested, they were taken to the Zhenru Public Security Sub-bureau for detention. According to the bandits, the ticket was hidden in a large boat next to the bamboo raft at Yongning Bridge outside Loumen in Suzhou. In addition to temporarily handing over the two bandits, Guo Kuangsheng and Liu Ziming, to the sub-bureau for custody, the detectives took Wang to Suzhou by express train that night. At about 9:00 PM that night, they rescued the two hostages, Jin Zishouchun and Ni Mubao's grandson Ah Er (Xiao Laohu), from Yongning Bridge outside Loumen, as well as Ouyang Renfu, who was in charge of "the boat" and "the ticket," and seized two pistols and one boat. They are still being interrogated by the Detective Team. It is expected that they will be sent to Suzhou for trial the day after tomorrow.

Economic Travel Agency Organizes Yixing Cave Tour 141

Yixing Shanquan Gengsang are famous ancient caves for thousands of years. They are the places where Master Shanquan and Zhang Guolao practiced during the Yao era. Gengsang is known for its greatness, and Shanquan is known for its exquisiteness, especially the water cave. Gengsang has a front cave and a back cave, and Shanquan has an upper cave, a middle cave, a front water cave, and a back water cave. Now, Yixing Shen Chunqiang has been operating for more than ten years. The places that ordinary people could not reach in the past are now flat and easy to walk. French Police Seize a Large Quantity of Red Pills 146

At No. 9 Rue Auliff

Ganslin (transliteration), a Western detective from the Chengdu Road Police Station of the Public Concession, and Chinese detective Ma Zhongrong, were patrolling the Chenjiabang area of Chengdu Road at 1 PM the day before yesterday when they saw a group of people acting suspiciously. Upon searching them, they found a package of red pills, totaling thirty-six, in their pockets. They were immediately taken to the police station. Interrogation revealed that his name was Wu Heshang, 27 years old, a local resident living at No. 9 Rue Auliff in the French Concession. He admitted to selling drugs. The detectives immediately took Wu to the French Police Station and reported the situation. Western detective Pu Quegu (transliteration), along with detective Cao Fuchang, deputy detective Wang Anming, and detective Jiang Huchen, rushed to the location and arrested a woman, Wu Zhou (25 years old, a local resident). Inside the house, they seized sixteen packages of red pills, each containing one thousand pills, totaling sixteen thousand pills. Interrogation revealed that the red pills were delivered by Qin Kun'gen (37 years old, a local resident), an accomplice living at No. 18 Rue Lanweiai. The detectives immediately rushed to the address and arrested Qin. Qin further stated that the red pills belonged to Ni Agou, the owner of the front building at No. 13 Huabao Lane, Huanghe Road, who manufactured them himself using a machine. The Chinese and Western detectives rushed to Huabao Lane to arrest Ni, but he had already fled upon hearing the news. According to Qin's statement, the manufacturing machine was located in the back building at No. 13 Liuhe Lane, Huanghe Road. They rushed to search it but only found two sieves used for making pills. Nothing else was found. Wu Zhou and Qin, along with the red pills and sieves, were taken to the police station and yesterday were sent to the First Criminal Court of the Special No. 2 District Court. Judge Xiong conducted a preliminary hearing. Because the police investigation was not complete, they requested a postponement. After questioning the defendants, the judge ordered them to be remanded in custody and granted a postponement for further investigation.

Discord Between Japanese Department Stores and Small Capital Shops 149

Japanese Merchants Opposing Each Other

The Authorities Have No Way to Adjudicate

According to the Japanese-language "Daily News," the Shenjiawan Industrial Department Store previously established a restaurant department, which caused discord with the Japanese restaurant industry association in the city. The association, from the standpoint of protecting its interests, discussed countermeasures. However, employees of the Industrial Department Store sent threats to the restaurant association, which further angered the association. They filed a complaint with the Consul General. The Industrial Department Store also planned to establish a barber shop and, with a somewhat forceful attitude, clashed with the barber industry. As a result, the conflict between the association members and the department store intensified. Last night, both sides held emergency meetings to discuss countermeasures. This is because of the sluggish economy, which makes it difficult for small-capitalists in various industries to survive due to the competition from department stores. Department stores are generally cheaper than other stores in any area. For example, beer is sold for 48 cents per bottle at the department store, while it is sold for 70 cents at restaurants. As a result, the operation of small capital is greatly affected. This type of opposition has become a social problem in Japan. Unfortunately, it has now occurred between Japanese merchants in Shanghai. The outcome of the dispute is difficult to predict.

According to the Japanese-language "Daily News," the Industrial Department Store has been established for one year. The most developed business of the store is the dining room, which averages around 6,500 yuan per day. The reason for its development is that the goods in the various affiliated departments are cheaper than those of ordinary independently operated small shops. For example, beer, sake, and sukiyaki (beef, bird, and fish hot pot) are particularly cheap, which caused conflict with the association. Both sides have their own arguments, and the Japanese authorities have no way to adjudicate. However, the cheap goods in the department store's dining room are due to the slightly cheaper wholesale prices, so the retail prices are also lower, which cannot be compared with stores that seek excessive profits.

A Girl Commits Suicide by Poisoning Due to Unfree Marriage 150

Chen Zhao, a widow from Zhenjiang residing at No. 80 Xiamen Road, had a daughter named Qiaoyun, 29 years old, with some beauty. Since childhood, she had been betrothed by her mother to the Wang family in her hometown as a daughter-in-law. However, recently, the girl's heart had opened, and she had fallen in love with Liu Shude in Shanghai, and they had made a vow of lifelong commitment. This made her very dissatisfied with the marriage arranged by her mother. A few days ago, she received a notice from the Wang family stating that they would choose an auspicious day for the wedding. Chen Zhao then told her daughter to quickly prepare her luggage and return to her hometown to fulfill the wedding ceremony. Upon hearing this, the girl was filled with resentment and suddenly had thoughts of ending her life. She secretly swallowed opium to commit suicide. Her mother caught a glimpse of her but it was too late. She was already moaning in bed. She was immediately sent to Guangren Hospital, but treatment was ineffective, and she soon died. The hospital reported to the Laozha Police Station, and detective Xie Guisheng went to investigate. He then took the body to the Ferry Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, accompanied by medical examiner Wei and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. Interrogation of Chen Zhao, the deceased's mother, revealed the previous situation. Guo concluded that the deceased, Chen Qiaoyun, a female, had died from opium poisoning. The body was released to her mother, Chen Zhao, who signed a statement to take it back for encoffining.

Fire at Yuanchang Road 151

One Injured in a Fall, Two Burned

Liu Mingxing, a 45-year-old blind man from Hubei, residing at No. 163 Yuanchang Road, Hongkou, made a living by lending money at usurious rates. Yesterday morning at around 5:30 AM, a fire broke out because a tenant downstairs was careless with fire. The fire quickly spread. The fire department rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm. As a result, one shop was burned down. When the fire was raging, Liu jumped from the building and broke his leg and fractured his back. His wife, Yu (46 years old), was burned all over her body. Also a girl, one of two landlords, was rescued from the fire but suffered burns to her head and hands. She was taken to the Shanghai Sanatorium by ambulance. Liu Mingxing was later taken to Tongren Hospital by police car for treatment.

Ninety-Eight Members of the Lawyers' Association Suggest Maintaining the Committee System Temporarily 152

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association, due to an order from the Ministry of Judicial Administration to amend its articles of association and restore the president-council system prior to the Republic of China year 16, has convened six general membership meetings, but each time the quorum was not met and the meeting was adjourned. It was decided to postpone the meeting for three weeks. However, ninety-eight current members have jointly proposed to maintain the provisions of the provisional articles of association regarding the committee system, and have requested that the resolution be decided by the general meeting and submitted to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for temporary approval to continue its use. The original text is transcribed below. Case: This Association received the Instruction No. 3517 from the Shanghai District Court, transferred by the Ministry of Judicial Administration, stating that the China Rule of Law Promotion Society reported that the Shanghai Lawyers' Association adopted the committee system, which is inconsistent with the provisions of Article 26 of the Lawyers' Regulations. It is requested that the Association be ordered to comply with the amendment. The Shanghai Lawyers' Association, due to special circumstances, previously presented a request to temporarily implement the committee system. Since it was a temporary expedient measure, it should still follow Article 26 of the Lawyers' Regulations and be amended. After receiving the above instruction, this Association formulated an amendment and included it in the agenda, convening a general membership meeting to submit it for discussion. However, the meeting failed to be convened five consecutive times, resulting in no resolution on this matter. The members stated that after this Association requested and was approved to implement the committee system, the Association's affairs have been progressing daily for eight years. Examining the past history, the work efficiency during the committee system was actually much higher than during the president system. The facts are all there and can be reviewed. Therefore, from the standpoint of this Association, there is absolutely no need to feel the necessity of amendment. Moreover, this Association has many members and heavy affairs, which cannot be compared with other associations. The special circumstances of changing to the committee system still exist. Since the announcement of the amendment, six meetings have been convened, but none have been successful. The direction of people's hearts can be measured. Since the Ministry of Judicial Administration temporarily approved the adoption in the past due to special circumstances, it must be able to appreciate the sentiments of the people and temporarily approve the continued adoption today, when the special circumstances still exist. Is it appropriate? Please decide. Proposers: Ding Zheming, Ding Qiwu, Wang Youling, Dong Kang, Zhang Yaozeng, Wu Kaisheng, Shen Junru, Wang Weizhen, Shi Liang, Chen Tingrui, Wu Guotai, Li Ming, Ge Zhiqin, Xu Wenrong, Yu Zhongluo, Li Shirui, Shan Yuhua, Xu Zuoliang, Che Bingrong, Zhu Fuju, Zhou Shiying, Yu Qinxiang, Yu Yuan, Guo Shouyi, Zheng Wentong, Yang Yuan, Pan Xi, Pan Zhensheng, and ninety-eight others signed and sealed.

Haimen Disaster Relief Representatives Arrive in Shanghai 153

Shen Yanmou, Xu Ruwen, Lu Xuzai, Xu Lisheng, and other representatives from the Haimen County Disaster Relief Committee arrived in Shanghai yesterday and will be soliciting donations from various parties in the coming days to save the starving refugees. According to the representatives, Haimen County has suffered from banditry and communism in the past four years, followed by floods, then locusts devouring the crops, and then continuous rain damaging the crops. Natural disasters and man-made disasters have been incessant, leading to widespread suffering and starvation. The drought this year has caused an unprecedented catastrophe. Of the six districts in the county, the affected area is approximately 1,467,289 mu, with an estimated total loss of 6,962,678 yuan, and a population of 373,328 disaster victims. There is no shortage of benevolent people in Shanghai, who care about these hundreds of thousands of hungry and drowning disaster victims, whether out of a desire to help the masses or out of concern for their hometown. It is believed that there will be generous donations.

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs Pays Attention to the People's Food Supply 155

Submitted a Request to the Municipal Government to Allocate Funds for Purchasing Rice

The weather has been dry this year, and the autumn harvest is expected to be poor. Not only are farmers suffering losses, but the future of the people's food supply is also greatly affected. Currently, the authorities in various provinces and cities are taking advantage of the autumn grain harvest to manage warehouses and store grain. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs in this city has also repeatedly forwarded central government instructions to pay attention to the people's food supply. Therefore, it has formulated measures and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval. According to Zhou Minggang, the director of the Food and Beverage Section of the Bureau, speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency, this city is a major industrial and commercial hub, and the issue of the people's food supply is of great importance. Although it is now the autumn grain harvest season, rice prices continue to rise. According to current market prices, each shi has risen to 13.5 yuan. If calculated in haihus, it will be around 18 yuan. By next spring, rice prices will inevitably rise further. The Bureau has now submitted a request to the Municipal Government to allocate funds for purchasing rice to regulate the people's food supply. If the Municipal Government can allocate the funds, it plans to purchase rice in rice-producing areas in the country, such as Hunan and Jiangxi, or to purchase from rice-producing countries abroad. Once the Municipal Government approves, it will proceed actively.

Education News

Suggestions for Improving Labor Education in Wuxi and Shanghai 169

The Ministries of Industry and Education have Ordered the Directors of Wuxi and Shanghai to Take Note

The Ministries of Industry and Education previously sent section chiefs Yang Fang and Zhong Lingxiu to inspect the implementation of labor education in Wuxi and Shanghai and to guide the organization of labor education experimental zones in both locations. Yan Shenyu (Wuxi), Pan Gongzhan (Shanghai), and others were appointed as chairmen of the steering committees for the labor education experimental zones in their respective areas. Section chiefs Yang and Zhong will present their inspection findings to the two ministries. Recently, the two ministries copied and forwarded the inspection report to Chairman Yan Shenyu (Wuxi) and Chairman Pan Gongzhan (Shanghai), instructing them to take note. The following are excerpts from the report regarding suggestions for improving the implementation of labor education in Wuxi and Shanghai:

Upon investigation, some of the labor education practices in Wuxi and Shanghai are effective and worthy of emulation, while others are poorly implemented and urgently need improvement. Several issues are detailed below: (1) "The steering committee for the labor education experimental zone should be organized quickly to serve as a central agency for promoting, guiding, and improving labor education." In Wuxi and Shanghai, those involved in labor education operate independently, without a unified central agency for guidance, planning, evaluation, and supervision. Although the Ministry has long promulgated the "Outline for the Implementation of Labor Education," providing some direction, the lack of supervision and evaluation has led to procrastination, hesitation, or the use of excuses to avoid implementation. It is imperative to establish the steering committee as soon as possible to serve as a central agency for guiding and supervising labor education in the area. This will allow for the establishment of specific measures, strict correction of errors, and the gradual implementation of well-regulated practices, leading to unobstructed progress and tangible results. (2) "Labor education provided by factories should focus on the workers themselves." Some factories in Wuxi and Shanghai provide labor education that complies with the provisions of Article 1 of the "Outline for the Implementation of Labor Education," aiming to enhance the knowledge and skills of the workers themselves. However, the majority run schools for the children of workers, while regarding the education of the workers themselves as optional and allowing them to make their own decisions. This violates the original intention of the "Outline for the Implementation of Labor Education" promulgated by the two ministries and should be corrected by encouraging factories to change their erroneous concepts and focus on improving labor education for workers. (3) "Factories should be required to develop plans for the phased implementation of labor education." Most of the labor schools or labor classes run by factories in Wuxi and Shanghai are perfunctory and lack planning. Furthermore, those that have not been established account for 70-80% of all factories. Factories should be urged to develop plans for phased implementation, allowing for periodic evaluation to achieve universalization and complete success. (4) "The curriculum of labor schools should be implemented separately in accordance with regulations." Article 5 of the "Outline for the Implementation of Labor Education" clearly stipulates the curriculum for labor schools or labor classes. However, an investigation of the labor schools run by factories in Wuxi and Shanghai reveals that the curriculum is often arbitrarily reduced, with students selecting only one or two subjects or adding irrelevant subjects. This is improper and should be corrected by urging factories to follow the regulations and teach the subjects separately, without arbitrary additions or subtractions. (5) The labor education department of the Experimental Public School attached to the Jiangsu Provincial Educational Institute in Wuxi and the public education center in the south gate of the city have well-planned and well-managed programs that can serve as models for those involved in labor education. Factories should be instructed to pay attention to emulate them to make improvements.

Minister of Education Wang Shijie Discusses the Purpose of the National Labor Exhibition 170

The Ministry of Education will compile a comprehensive list of the achievements of this year's National Vocational School and Elementary and Secondary School Labor Courses. The first item on the list is Minister Wang's discussion of the purpose of the achievements exhibition, followed by statistics on the types of exhibits and various charts, etc. The full text of Minister of Education Wang Shijie's discussion on the purpose of the National Vocational School and Elementary and Secondary School Labor Course Achievements Exhibition is recorded below:

In recent years, the government, recognizing the discrepancy between past educational facilities and the actual lives of the people, has been striving to correct this. In the educational goals announced by the central government, it has repeatedly emphasized cultivating the spirit of hard work and endurance among the people and enhancing their productive skills. The educational implementation measures promulgated by the government also identify "labor," "production," and "practicality" as the core of education at all levels. As a result, "manual training" in general schools is gradually being regarded as equally important as "brain training," and vocational education is gradually being regarded as equally important as general education in the entire educational system. In order to implement the central government's educational policies, the Ministry of Education has, in recent years, been actively paying attention to the establishment of labor courses in elementary and secondary schools, while also striving to improve vocational education throughout the country. For example, it has formulated standard measures for the establishment and funding of secondary schools in various provinces and cities in order to determine the proportion of vocational education funding and correct the past bias towards general secondary schools; it has stipulated procedures for promoting vocational education in various provinces, cities, and counties in order to determine the steps for implementation; it has formulated outlines for the registration and training of vocational school teachers in various provinces and cities in order to improve the quality of teachers; and it has promulgated outlines for the teaching subjects and hours of vocational schools, as well as outlines for the curriculum and equipment of vocational schools in order to show teaching standards, etc. These are all facilities that the Ministry of Education has been striving to promote vocational education in recent years.

However, it is necessary to conduct a thorough investigation to determine whether the recent achievements of various provinces and cities in promoting vocational education have reached the minimum standards expected by the government and whether they have realized the progress that is factually possible in each province and city. This year, the Ministry of Education has designated regions and assigned special commissioners to inspect vocational education and conduct on-site assessments. However, due to limitations in manpower and time, it has not been possible to conduct universal and detailed inspections, and the focus has been on the execution of laws and general conditions, with little detailed examination of actual teaching achievements. The purpose of holding this National Vocational School and Elementary and Secondary School Labor Course Achievements Exhibition is to review the actual achievements of vocational education and labor training in elementary and secondary schools in various provinces and cities.

This exhibition is an innovation in the history of education in our country and will have a significant impact on vocational education and labor training in elementary and secondary schools in the future. However, the colleagues of the Ministry of Education absolutely do not want to have the slightest exaggeration or embellishment. For this exhibition, we hope that it can meet the following conditions: First, it can represent the general achievements of ordinary times, rather than specially made products made temporarily; second, it can display scientific technology; third, it has practical value and can reflect the unity of school work and social production. Whether the exhibits actually meet the above conditions is something we hope visitors will carefully observe, and we especially hope that the results of their observations will be revealed to us so that those engaged in educational administration and school work can determine the path for future improvement.

City Education Association Requests the Aviation Association to Continue Handling Aviation Donations 176

The Association Will Also Continue to Raise Funds to Purchase the Shanghai School No. 2 Aircraft

The Shanghai Education Association has made considerable efforts to raise funds for aviation donations. Last year, it pioneered the purchase of the Shanghai School aircraft. This initiative prompted various organizations to make successive efforts, leading to the appearance of aircraft such as the Shanghai Merchant and Shanghai Worker. However, since this year, the aviation donation movement has gradually declined. The association believes that this movement should continue to be pursued unceasingly in order to avoid being criticized for a five-minute fever and to strengthen national defense. Therefore, it has decided to continue raising funds to purchase the Shanghai School No. 2 aircraft and has sent a letter to the China Aviation Association requesting it to continue handling aviation donations. An excerpt of the original letter is recorded below: Respected Sir, It has been investigated that the Aviation Association's aviation donations have been able to accumulate small amounts to prepare aircraft for national defense, and the results are gratifying. However, our country has a vast territory and must have a large number of aircraft installed and equipped to consolidate air defense and defend the country without any worries. Moreover, now that military reduction negotiations have broken down, imperialists are sharpening their swords and preparing for a second world war. All of our people must be inspired and excited, catch up quickly, and donate aircraft to help the government strengthen its air defenses in order to fulfill our national duties. In view of this, our association has submitted a discussion at the first joint meeting of directors and supervisors, and it has been decided that holding aviation donations is an urgent matter. In addition to our association having previously donated the Shanghai School No. 1 aircraft, we should continue to raise funds to purchase the Shanghai School No. 2 aircraft, and it has been unanimously resolved to urge your association to continue handling aviation donations to benefit national defense. This record is filed for your reference and action, and we hope to receive a reply.

City Education Bureau Formulates a Standard Form for Secondary Schools' Self-Use Student Registration Cards 177

The City Education Bureau instructed all secondary schools yesterday, stating: Upon investigation, each school's handling of student registration, the student's educational history, the process of handling registration, and the situation indicated by this bureau's review should all be recorded in detail within the school to facilitate checking and periodic review, so as to avoid any omissions. In past investigations of various schools, there has often been a lack of attention to this, causing students to be rejected at graduation due to procedures not meeting requirements, and the schools are at a loss as to why. The impact is not small. In view of this, and in order to remedy the situation, this bureau has formulated a student registration card for each school's self-use. Please imitate and apply it yourself. However, if the original method used is indeed excellent, it can also be used as a reference for improvement, to achieve perfection. The cards must be completed within one month of the arrival of this document. This bureau will send personnel to the schools at any time for spot checks. This order is for compliance.

Director of Gansu Education Department Shui Zi Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 178

Will Return to Nanjing Tonight

Shui Chuqin, Director of the Gansu Education Department, went to Beijing a few days ago to attend an inspection meeting, and to ask the educational authorities for instructions on policy direction and to raise local education funding. After completing his official duties, he and a secretary took the overnight express train to Shanghai the night before, arriving at the station at 8 AM yesterday morning and staying at the East Asia Hotel. A reporter from the Kwok Man News Agency met Mr. Shui at the hotel yesterday. According to him, he had no other tasks than to visit friends. However, he recently read a report about Tao Xingzhi's popularization of national education, which had very good methods. He would very much like to talk to him about it. If it is economical and effective, it would be very appropriate to try it in Gansu Province, as Gansu Province is poor and the people are poor, and the economy is extremely strained. All facilities have no way to start. He has repeatedly submitted to the Central Government requesting resignation, but has not been approved. However, while in office, he will still be responsible for everything. This trip south has received a lot of sympathy from the authorities for the request to allocate local education funding, who believe that this is an urgent matter at present. If nothing is done to improve or force education, the large number of out-of-school children in Gansu Province, which account for 10% of the population, will be a major hidden worry for the future of the nation. It is reported that Mr. Shui will not stay in Shanghai for long and will take the express train to Beijing tonight and then return to the province to preside over the department's affairs.

Huang's Chuanjing Study Offers Western Books 188

A Good Opportunity to Enrich the Library

Huang's Chuanjing Study, due to the expansion of its collection of Chinese classics, intends to transfer its collection of three major Western magazines, regardless of their original value, to domestic public and private libraries for safekeeping, or to exchange them for useful books. These include: (1) The China Economic Monthly, published by the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, a total of 84 volumes from the first issue to the end of last year. The contents all explore the production and sales of local products, as well as import and export statistics over the years, and major works on social economy. It is truly an important modern publication in our country. (2) The Chinese Science and Art Magazine, a total of 120 thick volumes from the first issue to the end of last year. It contains many translations of ancient and modern Chinese codes, poems, prose, novels, as well as inscriptions and techniques for appreciating fine objects. Each issue also has dozens of valuable color and monochrome pictures. (3) The Geographical Magazine published by the American Geographical Society, a total of 174 thick volumes from 1918 to June 1932. Each volume has one or two hundred color and monochrome photographs, and the text is mostly descriptive with little theory, all photographed and written by people who have experienced the situation firsthand, which is by no means comparable to those who construct theories behind closed doors. Regarding the situation in our border areas and inland areas, there are often detailed records, and many writers in various countries have adopted and compiled them as material for geographical books. The above three types are still being published and are all in perfect condition. If libraries or individuals wish to obtain a large number of reference books, they can write to Mr. Huang Qingzhi at the Accounting Department, Room 14, 3rd Floor, Shanghai Post Office for consultation.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 200

— (Cang Chang)

Hope is the bud; many great careers are built because hope sprouts and grows.

Don't ignore the small; dripping water can penetrate stone.

If someone recorded the history of every copper coin, I think there would be amazing insights.

Risheng Building 201

— Zhou Xian

The most prosperous place in China is naturally Shanghai. The most prosperous place in Shanghai is naturally Nanjing Road in the British Concession, also known as Great Horse Road. Speaking of the prosperous center of Great Horse Road, I think it should be Risheng Building.

That's right, Risheng Building is at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Zhejiang Road, and directly south is Hubei Road. If you take an aerial photo of Risheng Building from an airplane, I think the intersecting Nanjing and Zhejiang Roads, plus Hubei Road, might actually look like five winding dragons. Risheng Building is a teahouse with a very long history, originally called Five Dragons Risheng Building. Today, people simply call it Risheng Building and don't mention Five Dragons, which is a big mistake.

Risheng Building occupies a pivotal position in the north-south and east-west transportation hub. All kinds of vehicles and pedestrians come and go in large numbers, so some people say that at least 100,000 people pass by Risheng Building every 24 hours. Although there is no precise statistical evidence for this, in my opinion, this number may still be an underestimate.

The Sincere and Wing On department stores face each other across from Risheng Building, and Wing On is still building a new building between Zhejiang and Hubei Roads. After its completion, this prosperous center of Shanghai will naturally become more magnificent. But I hope that the area near the east corner will permanently maintain its original state. One reason is to permanently preserve the Five Dragons Risheng Building, and the other is that I fear that if five large buildings are erected, without tobacco, sweets, fruits, snack shops, and everything else, such as sugar-roasted chestnut stalls and pan-fried bun stalls, there will no longer be the ability to attract pedestrians.

The Interest of the Window 202

— Yi Wen

People's temperament is easily affected by the environment, and even the environment can determine people's will. Therefore, Mencius' mother chose her neighbors. For the sake of changing an environment, it will make people feel a new interest. We don't mind the trouble of moving, moving from a larger old residence into a small new residence. In the new residence, there is just enough space for two beds, two tables, and one stool. It can only seat one person, and you can only work on the bed. When walking, you have to learn to walk sideways like a crab. It's so small that it seems a bit annoying. However, the scenery from the window is not bad. The silk vines on the wall spread to the window, hanging down weakly, covering one-third of the window. The trees on Huayuan Road, seen from the window, have very deep and dense green shade. Occasionally, one or two fluttering fallen leaves fly down. The nearby and distant houses appear faintly, quietly, without the creaking of wheels, without the hustle and bustle of people. It's unexpected that bustling Shanghai actually has such a quiet area. In the evening, the twilight shrouds the somber trees. Only one street lamp is like a radiant star. After the lights in the room are turned off, the light from the street lamp shines through the glass, illuminating the wall with a blurred shadow of the silk vines. When I wake up in the morning, the sun shines directly on our window, and the mottled shadows of the trees on the wall are like a silver screen. Another unique feature is the transom, which uses lead sheets instead of glass, with a round hole cut in the middle. The sunlight passes through the round hole, illuminating the wall with an exceptionally bright white circle. This white circle, together with the mottled shadows of the trees, in a frame that is almost entirely black, can also be seen, facing each other, it is truly impossible to tell what is real and what is fake. Gradually, it moves until it disappears. In short, although our new home is small, the interest of the window is not small. The interest of the window can more than compensate for the hardship of the narrow room, so we live here very comfortably.

The Mystery of the Lock 203

A Brief History of the Handshake 204

— (Zhong)

The handshake was originally a European custom, but now it has spread all over the world. In our country, it is also very popular. People, whether old or young, male or female, shake hands with each other when they meet, replacing nods, bows, and cupped-fist salutes. But few people know the origin of the handshake. I will now write down what I heard from a Western friend for everyone to see:

Originally, this event happened in the ancient Western world. At that time, Europeans were brave and straightforward. When going out, they always wore swords at their waists as protective gear. Because people in ancient times occasionally had disagreements in their common life, they had to draw their swords to demonstrate to each other. If one party had a sincere expression of regret, the other party would extend their right hand to shake the other party's hand. If the other party sympathized, they would also extend their right hand to indicate that they were back on good terms.

From this simple historical fact, we can understand the origin of the handshake. However, for modern people, even Europeans, where handshakes originated, this event has become as common as nodding and bowing, without much significance. Only on football fields and tennis courts, when athletes on both sides compete, they look like enemies. When the competition ends, they extend their hands to shake each other, which still has some of the style of the ancient Western Europeans!

Little Western Paradise 205

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Five: Fawning and Smiling, Holding Up a Lamp to Illuminate Her Haggard Appearance, Driven by a Hungry Stomach, Applying Powder to Learn Flirtation

However, Huanhua misunderstood. He thought that Jia Duocai was admiring his beauty, and he smiled from time to time, biting his shallow lips, and glancing sideways at Jia Duocai with his deep-set eyes. The more Jia Duocai saw those affectations, the more uncomfortable he felt, so he turned his face away and talked to Li Shilian. Yang Huanhua heard that Jia Duocai was a banker, and he was very willing to approach him. He didn't want to, after only saying a few words about their friendship as fellow villagers, Jia Duocai ignored him. Want to connect a little electricity with him? He turned his face away again. Could he walk over and turn his face around? He looked down at his bosom for a while and had an idea. He borrowed a pack of cigarettes placed on the table and held it in his hand, smiling and asking many people, "Does anyone smoke?" Guo Dunpin knew what to do and said to him, "Offer Mr. Jia one." Huanhua didn't wait for him to answer and had already pinched a cigarette with his three thin fingers and sent it to Jia Duocai. At this time, he could no longer refuse and had to stand up and take the cigarette. Huanhua pressed on even harder, reaching into his pocket to take out a box of matches, struck one, and stretched it forward to light Jia Duocai's cigarette. He really didn't expect him to be so polite, so he hadn't put the cigarette in his mouth yet. Huanhua really had that kind of patience, holding a lit match between two fingers, bending slightly, waiting quietly. Only after Jia Duocai held the cigarette in his mouth did he light it for him. The flame of the match was already burning near his fingers. Jia Duocai, seeing his attentiveness, naturally felt a little embarrassed, so he smiled at him and said, "Everyone who comes here is a guest, you don't have to be so polite." He smiled and returned to his seat. Guo Dunpin, sitting on the bed, was a little farther away. He thought to himself, "Old Jia probably hasn't seen him clearly yet, so he's still so indifferent." (74)

Records of Ethereal Incense 206

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

The pervasive tranquility and antique air, the tall, lush trees, and the lack of floral and avian embellishments here are almost entirely natural. How could human effort ever transform them? Unless all the furnishings, flowers, trees, birds, and so forth of the Forbidden City in Beijing were moved here, it would be impossible to conceal their original rustic and empty true face. Even if they could be concealed, it would only amount to applying a layer of cosmetic adornment; their essence could never be altered!

I finally trembled so violently that I could not linger on the veranda and hastily returned to my own chamber.

Four of us slept together in this chamber. Besides my sister and me, there were two other female officials. At that time, all three of them were already sound asleep because the illusions of terror and unease had never invaded their minds. They could easily drift off into peaceful dreams. But what about me? I was still apprehensive, fearing that a great disaster was about to befall us, and I didn't even have the courage to blow out the candle. Although I myself understood that this was a foolishly ridiculous thought, could there really be any unfortunate events in this heavily guarded palace that would befall us? There was no need to doubt; it was absolutely impossible! Moreover, I also knew that at this time, the Empress Dowager was sleeping very comfortably in her palace in the main hall. Since the Empress Dowager felt no fear or unease, then I, as her attendant female official, should naturally not be intimidated in the slightest, striving to emulate her calm demeanor. Why should I continue to be suspicious and torment myself?

In this state of self-contradiction and fluctuating thoughts, I quietly climbed into bed alone. When I first got into bed, I firmly believed that I wouldn't be able to sleep soundly tonight, perhaps not even able to close my eyes. But after tossing and turning in bed for a while, I don't know how I made up my mind, but I actually closed my eyes and slept very comfortably, not even knowing when it was dawn. (184)

Local Customs and Anecdotes

A Dictionary of Shanghai Vernacular 207

— Shanghai General News Agency

Dialects differ from place to place, and those not born and raised locally often find them difficult to understand. The Shanghai dialect is especially more complex than other dialects. There are quite a few expressions that have sounds but no corresponding written characters. However, there are also some that can be expressed in writing and whose origins can be traced. Here are a few examples, to give a glimpse.

毛病 (Máo bìng) - Fault; bad habit. Commonly used to describe a habit as a fault. The term appears in Huang Shangu's writings: "This is the fault of the people of Jingnan."

關子 (Guān zi) - Crux; key point. It refers to the crucial point of a matter. The term originates from the Book of Tang. When Li Fengji was in power, he had eight close associates, including Zhang Youxin and Li Zhongyan, and another eight who attached themselves to them. All held important positions, and people at the time called them the "Eight Gatekeepers and Sixteen Sons." Anyone seeking a favor had to bribe the "gatekeepers" first before reaching Li Fengji, and then everything would be accomplished. The common expression "賣關子 (mài guān zi)" - to keep someone in suspense - refers to hiding the crucial information and refusing to reveal it. The origin is likely the same.

垃圾 (Lā jī) - Garbage; trash. Formerly written as "拉扱 (lā chā)," referring to accumulated dirt, debris, and filth. However, the Meng Liang Lu (Dream Log Records) mentions "boats carrying garbage and manure on various rivers," indicating that the term has been in use for a long time.

空頭 (Kōng tóu) - Empty; unsubstantial. Refers to something that is empty and lacks substance. Found in the History of the North: Biography of Hülü Jin: "An empty head should be killed."

面子 (Miàn zi) - Face; prestige. Commonly refers to having glory as having "face." Old Book of Tang: Biography of Zhang Jun: "Only after the bandits are pacified will there be face."

豬玀 (Zhū luó) - Pig. A term used by Shanghainese to scold people, actually a corruption of "豬婁 (zhū lóu)." Zuo Zhuan: "Once you have settled your female pigs, why not return to find your male pig?"

正經 (Zhèng jīng) - Proper; upright. Refers to not engaging in deception or pursuing wickedness. Book of Songs, chapter on "Gentleman Yang Yang," commentary says: "The constant joy of the royal chamber is the proper way of the wind."

惡 (È) - Excrement. Commonly refers to dung, pronounced with a falling tone. History of the Former Han Dynasty, Biography of the King of Changyi: "Such things are like bluebottle fly dung." Yan Shigu's annotation says: "That is, feces. King Goujian of Yue tasted the excrement for the King of Wu."

頭家 (Tóu jiā) - Banker; owner. Refers to the person who sets up a gambling game to collect a commission. Also called "抽頭 (chōu tóu)" - to take a cut. Tang Yinghua's "Rhapsody on Playing Sugoroku" says: "Seeing those defeated in the game, not acting as the head in the game." Also, Su Dongpo recorded that a young man who gambled and won a thousand gold pieces without losing found a formula that said, "Only ask for the cut." That is, to take a commission.

差路 (Chā lù) - Wrong path. Refers to something that is not proper. Tang poetry says, "There are many wrong paths in front of the Pine Tree Rock."

擡舉 (Tái jǔ) - To lift up; to support. Refers to assisting. Bai Letian's poem "High Lotus": "Standing tall, lifting itself up."

打孛 (Dǎ bèi) - To tease; to play tricks on. Commonly written as "打棚 (dǎ péng)," referring to making fun of others to amuse oneself. Wu Xia Proverbs couplet: "Let you come to tease."

薄相 (Báo xiàng) - To play around; to amuse oneself. Commonly written as "白相 (bái xiàng)," also written as "孛相 (bèi xiàng)," a common vernacular in Wu region, meaning to play around. Huang Shangu's letter to Elder Fan says: "Han Shi goes to the neighboring school every day, just to protect his play." Also, Zhao Xianyou's poem "Visiting Mount Hua and Sending to Yuan Yuzhi": "The mountain gods also play tricks on people."

黄六 (Huáng liù) - Fake; false. Refers to something that is deceptive and not real. Shen Zinan's Yilin Hui Kao (Collected Examinations of the Forest of Arts) says: "Huang Chao walked sixth and was often deceitful, so those who deceive people are called Huang Liu."

交關 (Jiāo guān) - Very much; a lot. Commonly refers to something that is extremely numerous, from Jin Shu, Biography of Pei Xiu: "Dealing with numerous human affairs."

温暾 (Wēn tūn) - Lukewarm. Refers to something that is warm but not very hot. Bai Letian's poem "Kaiyuan Temple": "The pool water is warm and lukewarm"; also Wang Jian's Palace Poem: "The new clear grass color is warm and lukewarm."

作人情 (Zuò rén qíng) - To give a gift; to do someone a favor. Refers to giving someone something as a gift, from Du Gongbu's poem "Fried cakes as gifts."

訂真 (Dìng zhēn) - To ascertain the truth; to be serious. Commonly refers to being serious as "訂真 (dìng zhēn)," also corrupted to "頂真 (dǐng zhēn)," originating from Wang Chong's Lun Heng (Balanced Discourses), which "ascertains the truth and falsity and distinguishes the reality from the fiction of the books of the world."

乾癟 (Gān biě) - Dried up; withered. Refers to something that is dry and withered, found in Qi Xiu Lei Lan (Seven Repairs Classified Orchid) poetry, "The prime minister does business, only uses Huang Cai leaves, the west wind rises overnight and dries up." Commonly refers to beggars as "癟 (biě)," saying that they are cold without clothes, hungry without food, and without a dwelling, meaning that the three things of clothing, food, and shelter are all dried up and without a place to land.

欵乃 (Kuǎn nǎi) - Sound of oars. Pronounced like "ǎi ǎo," the sound made by a porter when carrying a heavy load, or the sound of oars, either responding to oneself or responding to each other. Originally a boatman's song, Zhu Xi distinguished it as: "The oars of the boat match each other," now people call it in reverse by mistake.

連忙 (Lián máng) - Hastily; hurriedly. Refers to being eager to complete work. Zhu Xi's Collected Poems: "Hurry to add thatch to the roof, quickly finish the field."

㜘 (Chū) - Good; beautiful. Shanghainese call something beautiful as "㜘 (chū)," pronounced like "wū." Ji Kang's "Rhapsody on the Qin": "Or complains and hesitates."

Equalization Tax Calculation Method

Why Does Silver Still Flow Out?

Why Is There Still Hesitation When It Flows Out?

The Answer Is Not Difficult to Find

Tracing back to when the US government raised the price of silver and implemented a silver purchasing policy, the outflow of silver in our country was extremely large, so our government had no choice but to implement an increase in silver export taxes, and at the same time, levied an equalization tax, with the Ministry of Finance instructing the Central Bank to list and announce it daily. The outflow of silver was able to be stopped. Recently, the equalization tax on silver set by the Central Bank is relatively loose, which is because the Ping Shi Committee followed the request of foreign banks to regulate the market. Looking at Saturday, the equalization tax announced by the Central Bank was 6.25%, which was based on the British exchange rate of 1 shilling 5 pence 6875 as the flat price. In terms of the exchange market, the formal transaction of the British exchange rate was 1 shilling 4 pence, with a difference of more than 1.5 pence, which is the difference between the London and Shanghai silver markets. In other words, if the Shanghai banking community loaded silver to the UK, after deducting the taxes to be paid, they could still obtain a gross profit of more than 1.5 pence. Moreover, the payment of the equalization tax has also been changed to be calculated on the date of customs declaration, which is why the banks are happy to load and export. However, foreign banks are still worried that after a unified supply, the local exchange market will suddenly harden, and the overnight British silver will suddenly rise sharply, so there is still hesitation, and the shipment of silver can also be slightly restrained. Recently, it has been thought that the silver tax cannot control the outflow of silver, but they do not know that there is still this reason. In addition, even if the banks do not ship, looking at the standard gold price, they are still leaking almost entirely, so it can be seen that only starting from the currency is not a fundamental solution. Short sellers then covered their positions, leading to a slight increase. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, due to the rapid decline in the flour market that morning, market sentiment became extremely weak, leading to a surge in selling pressure and a sharp drop in prices. As a result, this month's contract fell by 7 cents, December's by 6 cents, January's by 7 cents, and February's by 9 cents. The spot wheat market saw no demand from factories and was quiet.

Chicago wheat, the matter of importing French wheat, has become a thing of the past. The hedging resulting from the fire in the Yamaha warehouse has had an increasingly strong influence on foreign markets, causing prices to rebound. In addition, strong demand for spot goods and unfavorable crop news have contributed to the rise.

Longs Recoup Gains, Floating Shorts Add Positions

Yesterday in the flour market, after the morning opening, prices for all months generally showed a sharp decline, with foreign wheat quoted at around 34 cents higher for Chicago and 23 cents higher for Canada. When the market opened in the afternoon, the trend stabilized slightly, and trading between both sides became clearer. Many profited from recouping gains, while new longs still entered the market, resulting in a temporary stalemate. As a result, this month's contract fell by 3.5 cents compared to the previous week, December's by 4 cents, February's by 3.5 cents, February's by 3.25 cents, March's by 4.25 cents, and April's by 3.75 cents.
