Free Talk

Realistic and Romantic 217

— Qi

Regardless of how literary historians divide literary trends into realism and romanticism, in literary practice, these two tendencies each have different artistic and social contents under different historical conditions, and they are often intertwined and cannot be mechanically separated. The creation of the same writer can contain both realistic and romantic elements. Even the most outstanding realistic writers sometimes inject elements of fantasy into reality, which is not uncommon in literary history.

In Shakespeare's plays, we see the appearance of Hamlet's father's ghost, terrible monsters patrolling the stage, and places where reality is exaggerated to a terrible extent. Balzac's "The Magic Skin" is said to provide a clearer understanding of French society at that time than any scientific research, but "The Magic Skin" is a Fantastic story. Gogol's masterpiece "The Overcoat" features ghosts stripping pedestrians of their overcoats at night. The protagonist of "The Nose" sees his lost nose riding in a carriage down the street, and even claims to be a fifth-rank civil servant. "Viy" is even a terrifying ghost story that makes your hair stand on end. However, this amazing combination of romantic fantasy and realistic depiction did not prevent these writers from being the greatest realists in literary history.

The old-fashioned distinction between realism and romanticism is unreliable. Dinamov, in an article on Shakespeare, pointed out the correct view of realism, which is worth our reference. Now let me quote Dinamov's words as follows:

"The evaluation of Shakespeare is not based on his external appearances of realism, but what is important is that Shakespeare did not look at reality from an idealist point of view. In his intention, in his content, and in the nature of his works, he is a realist. He utilized all kinds of literary and dramatic forms and genres, from comedy to tragedy, from tragedy to light stories, without ever treating objective reality as a simple reflection of the 'spirit'. His basis is fundamentally the surrounding world, ready-made rather than fabricated."

From this passage, we can see the standard of realism. If a writer's fundamental understanding of reality does not start from abstract subjective concepts but from reality and its own objective laws, then even if his works have places where reality is fantasized, they are still realistic works. On the contrary, romantic literature deals with reality with a thoroughly subjective, idealistic attitude. Fantasy, the desire for fantasy, is the source of romanticism. In the eyes of romanticists, fantasy is reality. Replacing gray reality with romantic fantasy is actually just an escape from reality. Romanticism as a trend is exactly this kind of thing.

Progressive literature should inherit the spirit of realism and stand firmly on reality, there is no doubt about this. However, at the same time, it must step over the boundaries of the old realism and regard romanticism as an inevitable aspect of its artistic creation. Here, romanticism is only a component part of realism, and not a trend that opposes realism. Romantic elements are present in true life. If we take a deep perspective on the positive side of life, we will surely find many heroic themes that are hard to believe.

The literature of old realism is non-heroic. It is characterized by a preference for the dark side of life. What it writes is all the ugliness, corruption, and hypocrisy of society. These writers cannot write "noble and beautiful things." The characters in their pens are mostly Philistines who do not have bright ideas and good deeds. Therefore, the more realistic their crops are, the more they show a gloomy and dim color, lacking the romantic and heroic atmosphere that can make people happy and inspired. This atmosphere is fully expressed in progressive realistic works. Because only progressive writers can delve into the positive aspects of life and find facts that are both moving and heroic.

"Realism is about accurately conveying typical characters in typical environments in addition to being detailed and authentic," this is a profound statement. Therefore, writers must have the ability to typify and generalize life phenomena. What they want to express is not life itself, but rather the truth about life. The typical thing is not modern, it can be picked up and obtained easily, but it is extracted and synthesized by the author from many things that are typical, essential, and common. Don Quixote or Hamlet do not really exist, but Shakespeare and Cervantes took the most typical qualities, habits, tastes, hopes, beliefs, grammar, etc. from many people and unified them in these two characters, so everyone feels that some of Don Quixote or Hamlet's elements are within their own blood. This kind of generalized typicality, even if it is exaggerated to a very romantic degree, still has artistic authenticity.

Artistic generalization is sometimes simply a "premonition." The author takes a secret, undeveloped, or embryonic fragment from reality, and points it out to people in an exaggerated form before they are aware of it, so the essence of that fragment is more typical and clearer. When "nihilism" had not yet become a major trend in Russian society, and Turgenev described a typical nihilistic character in "Fathers and Sons," contemporary critics regarded it as something that the author had imagined. They did not know that it was precisely the artistic generalization of reality.

Artistic generalization is not a simple representation of facts. Without creative imagination or fantasy, it is impossible to transform realistic materials into works of art. The kind of fantasy used by romanticists to escape reality and wander into ethereal realms cannot occupy a position in progressive realistic works, Needless to say. But fantasy itself is not a bad thing, and it can be said that people who cannot fantasize are stupid. Progressive writers must look at reality in the historical movement, find aspects with positive significance in the development of the times from reality, and express the future outline of those aspects. He must not only depict what already exists in reality, but also depict what may exist in reality. This relies on a rich imagination. However, such fantasy does not contradict the progress of reality, but can encourage people to strive to realize it. When literary works are permeated with this element of fantasy, they are likely to have romantic colors. And this kind of romanticism is rooted in reality and has the effect of illuminating and enriching reality.

To step over the boundaries of the surface of reality, delve into reality, synthesize reality, and achieve a true reflection of the essence of reality, this requires not only a correct worldview, but also a deep insight into reality and a great freedom of imagination.

"Check!" 218

— TK

Mayfly 219

— Dong Meng

When I was reading under the lamp, many mayflies flew around and collided. After several disturbances, they landed on the paper. By the next day, the bodies of these little things were lying in formation on the white paper, like irregularly inlaid patterns.

A friend said that mayflies are born in the morning and die in the evening. The lifespan of these little things is probably not very long. However, according to Emerson's mysterious lines of poetry, looking at a world in a grain of sand. Then their years of existence can also be said to be infinite. Although the universe is large, it is extremely small compared to other planets. Taking animals as an example, many dull and ignorant things, such as turtles and elephants, are also much older than humans. If we don't want to exaggerate ourselves? Then! The age of the earth is extremely short compared to many other planets. Comparing the two, one cannot help but feel discouraged and have a sense of living in the evening and dying.

However, human beings are ultimately spiritual things, and this is what makes them superior to all things. Mayflies are at most microorganisms. Look how small their form is! A Chinese poet has a wonderful metaphor: saying that mayflies shake big trees, it is often seen that they overestimate themselves. Among human beings, there is no such situation. Even if they fight each other, there are discords, struggles, or even cruel killings. But they always choose opponents that they can touch, and push, exclude, and trample on them; it can also be said to be shaking; but what is being shaken is their own kind. Moreover, they have already decided on their target before they even start.

People Who Drink Morning Tea 220

— Yin Guang

Besides the family, in Sichuan, the teahouse is probably the only place where people can find solace. I have seen many people who have developed an addiction, an inseparable indulgence, to this place that slowly erodes a person's life and energy, much like an opium addiction.

As soon as they crawl out of their bedding, they don't even bother to button up their clothes. They throw on their garments, slip on their shoes, and, coughing all the way, head to the teahouse. Sometimes, they arrive so early that the tea stove has only just been lit. The reason for this early arrival is sometimes because they discovered a piece of news worth telling people during the night. As soon as they open their eyes, they feel they cannot hold it in. Other times, it is simply because they heard an unusual noise from the street or a neighbor's house late at night while in bed, and they want to find out what happened to satisfy their curiosity.

However, even if it is not for these reasons, but because their habits have gone awry, this will not discourage them. They can sit in their usual spot in the dimness of dawn and doze off for a while. Or, they can try to glean some unexpected stories that they missed from the server's mouth with a few simple, vague questions.

"So late... Did you sleep late?"

"Strange things happened again in Water Alley," the server explains. "They just left that pile of junk on the doorstep..."

"Heh, I heard the giggling there," the customer laughs in satisfaction.

Of course, if the server curtly replies, "It's still early," they will quickly drift back to sleep until the pitiable person who wakes up before the night watchman falls asleep calls out, "The tea is ready!" Then, they will respond from their throats, "Humph," or nod slightly. However, even if they are silent, once the server calls out, their duty is fulfilled, and they each go about their work.

When they realize that the tea is ready, they always first use two fingers to dab a little on the corners of their eyes. Then, along the edge of the bowl, they blow a long breath to clear away the charred tea stems and broken leaves floating on the surface. They then drink down most of the bowl in one gulp. Then, puffing on their fire pipe, they cough and wheeze, forming something like a question mark. Only when other customers sit down in the teahouse does the first person to arrive at the teahouse appear to be alive. They perk up and, in a slow tone, report the story told by the server, interspersed with sighs and comments.

"It's still that bad thing that's no good, hitting and acting crazy when it sees people."

"If the bitch doesn't wag its tail, the dog won't get on its back!" another person echoes.

When this kind of talk can be brought to a close, the reporter yawns, rubs his eyelids, and mutters to the tea stove, "I haven't washed my face yet." So, the server drags a stool and places it in a convenient spot near the family seating area and brings over some water for washing. This way, it is not necessary to change the squatting position in order to wash one's face. One only needs to turn slightly to the side and stretch out both hands. However, if one has not yet participated in the conversations of other tea drinkers, washing one's face can take a very long time.

"You are not wronging him at all with your words. What I saw was even uglier. For example..." The washcloth, just raised by the fingers, falls back into the washbasin.

Sometimes, the server has to change the water in the washbasin before they can complete this very difficult task. Then, while slipping on their shoes and buttoning their buttons, they stroll over to the rice wine vendor across the street, bending over to examine the items on the carrying pole, and then, pointing their finger, they carefully instruct, word by word:

"Listen clearly? - Add an egg. A fresh one. Good, this one will do. You look at it for me..."

When the small vegetable vendors start calling out their wares along the chilling street market, they always buy some bean sprouts as usual, pile them on the tea table, and pick off the roots one by one, as finely as if they were embroidering. From their expressions, this is also a gesture close to extravagance. Once the vegetables are picked clean, the children at home will come and take them back, without them having to move a step; they only need to give the same old instructions:

"Don't talk about it, - add a little more vinegar, stir-fry it a little raw, got it!"

At breakfast time, they do not go home until the people at home have urged them three or five times. They slowly take the tea bowl to the middle of the tea table, ask the server to take care of it, and say they will come back after eating. All the while, they talk to the tea drinkers reluctantly, as if they are very unwilling to leave.

"And then what?"

"And then what, it wasn't admitting that he was wrong."

"I told you long ago, let him eat a little chili; I feel refreshed... "

By this time, the entire morning has been spent. But they don't feel sorry at all. In fact, they didn't even think about it. Once their stomachs are full, there is still a lot of time waiting for them, wasted like a wealthy person using their wealth.

Here, I only hope that the current unrest will not disturb them.

Tomorrow (1) 221

— (Written by Joseph Conrad) Translated by Wu Xiangyu

Captain Hagberd was not a popular character in the port of Colebrook. He wasn't from around here. The reasons he used to live here weren't too mysterious - he told them to people openly - but those reasons were ridiculously unbelievable. He obviously had some money, because he had bought a piece of land and built two very cheap, unsightly yellow brick houses. He lived in one himself and rented the other to Joshua, Javvil - blind Javvil, a shipbuilder - who had a bad reputation as a domestic tyrant.

The two houses shared a wall, and the small front gardens were separated by iron fences; the small back patios were separated by wooden fences. Besson, Miss Javvil, seemed to have a designated right to dry her tablecloth, blue rags, or a skirt in the middle.

'That'll rot the wood, Besson, my girl,' the captain said gently from his side of the wooden fence, every time he saw her exercising that prerogative.

She was a tall woman; the wooden fence was low, and she could rest her elbows on top of it. Her hands must have been red after she'd washed some clothes, but her forearms were white and beautiful. She always silently looked at her father's landlord - this meaningful silence was accompanied by an attitude of cordial anticipation.

'That'll rot the wood,' Captain Hagberd repeated. 'For you, I know this is just a careless, unintentional habit. Why don't you hang a rope in the back patio?'

Miss Javvil didn't say anything about this either - she just passively shook her head. In her back patio on one side, there was a bed of black soil, surrounded by stones, in which she grew a few flowers in her spare time, which looked very prosperous, like leisurely foreign ones; and on the other side of the wooden fence, wild flowers grew knee-high, and Captain Hagberd only showed a straight, healthy body, wrapped in a number one head-to-toe canvas suit. Using this color, this coarse, special material that he chose to make clothes, people looked at him - this was a silent marker of his current observation - just like a petrified man turned to bluestone standing upright in a wasteland not big enough for a good billiard room. In short, he was a huge stone man, with a red and beautiful face, a blue and lifeless eye, and a beard that drooped to his chest, which the people of Colebrook had never seen him cut or shave.

Seven years ago, Colebrook's famous comedian, the barber, happened to be proudly sitting in the saloon of the "New Hotel" on the seafront one day when the captain also went there to buy an ounce of tobacco. The barber playfully asked him when he could do his business. The captain replied very seriously, "I think, next month". After Captain Hagberd took out a halfpenny from the handkerchief tucked into his cuff to pay, he walked out. As soon as the door closed, the barber laughed. 'This old guy and a young man are about to walk into my shop hand in hand for a haircut. The tailor will soon have business, the barber will have business, and the candle shop will soon have business; good times are coming to Colebrook, they're coming, definitely. He used to answer "next week", but now he says "next month", maybe soon, I think, he'll say "next spring".'

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Great Assembly for World Peace Prayer 222

— Qiong Sheng

In this world where gunpowder depots are scattered and the smell of gunpowder permeates, it is time for compassionate people and diplomats who "cherish peace" to take the lead. For example, the peace prayer meeting held by the Roman Pope not long ago, and the peace prayer meetings held by General Superintendent Cai Ning in Peiping and other places after he came to China, all caused a sensation and spread far and wide. As for French Foreign Minister Barthou, who sacrificed his life in the Marseilles tragedy and worked harder for "peace", and former British Foreign Minister Henderson, who won the Nobel Peace Prize for his efforts in "disarmament", they are all outstanding figures.

However, in this wave of economic panic, the world's great powers are competing to find markets and joining forces to divide colonies. China, with its "vast land and abundant resources", has long become the main target of plunder by various imperialisms. No matter who wins or loses the war, China will be sacrificed. The trampling during the war and the slaughter after the war will all benefit the remaining land and 400 million people of China. Thinking of the trampling and fate that the descendants of the Yellow Emperor are bound to encounter, it is truly "chilling to the bone". Our opposition to war and support for peace is not to save some "human catastrophe" with "humanitarianism", but to take our own liberation as a practical benefit. The main purpose is here.

However, the inevitable trend of imperialism is to use war to solve the problem of "redistributing the world". This is the inevitable conclusion under the current social organization. Asking them not to go to war by means of "peace prayer" is no different from advising Zhang Xianzhong not to kill people. Asking them not to plunder colonies is like persuading a cat not to bite mice. If we, who have been regarded as "meat on the chopping board", want to find a way to national independence and liberation from "peace prayer", it is purely like a prisoner who has been sentenced to death, hoping for salvation from God to comfort ourselves.

Naturally, the "Great Assembly for Peace Prayer" has become a manifestation of this "progress". However, true peace, I am afraid, cannot be solved simply by the four characters of "peace prayer".

Flower Girl 223

— Lu Yin Quan

Autumn is ethereal, like a wisp of ethereal light cloud, flickering in the deep silver sea of the dark west sky, quietly rippling in, and now quietly rippling away again. In just a moment, perhaps we will not be able to see the remnants of autumn. When autumn comes, I don't have any special feeling. It's a bit strange to say, sometimes I don't even feel the existence of autumn. But now that it is about to disappear, I am somewhat reluctant. Even though I know that the emotion of reluctance will never be able to hold back the passage of time, my stubborn heart still insists on doing so; people, how foolish they are.

Others say that autumn is hidden in the scarlet maple leaves

Page 18

in the sharp claws of fat crabs, but I, perhaps you won't even believe it, realize the existence of autumn from the cry of a night-blooming jasmine flower girl outside the window, and at the same time, I feel the fall of late autumn in this cry. This wisp of sorrowful light sound is indeed full of the gloom of autumn. No, it's not just a little gloom, it's simply the whole of autumn.

Every day is like this, when I return from outside, reading some newly arrived magazines by the window, or picking up a pen to write, a rather haggard cry, from downstairs, like the breath of deep autumn, lightly floats over:

--Selling night-blooming jasmine!

This short cry, even without musical rhythm, bursts out with such a large amount of sorrow as autumn from this cry. My originally very tranquil heart is now inevitably depressed by this sound. Even if the cry has floated away, even if I can't hear it anymore, a lead-like blockage still presses on my heart, I don't know when this blockage will dissolve?

At the beginning of the new autumn, the flower girl's cry for sale seems to be louder, but now it seems to be gradually withering as autumn grows old. I really don't understand how such a haggard sound can escape from the lips of a beautiful young girl? Does she not have youth? Youth, disappeared in the weaving of the lifeline.

For a little pity and sympathy, I always listen to this mournful voice every day, adding some light sorrow to the quiet stream of life, it is also needed.

The deeper autumn is, the weaker her voice becomes. But today, how is it that I can't hear this cry? Is she not coming to sell night-blooming jasmine? I think, perhaps she disappeared along with the late autumn.

And a lead block still presses on my heart, even if a faint sorrow ripples on the corner of the building.

In the Park 224

— Zhou Han

Occasionally happy, I wanted to go to the park to bask in the sun. - Living in a house without sun, I am yearning for the sun as if I have fallen in love.

The park is already full of autumn colors: chrysanthemums can be seen everywhere. There are chrysanthemums on the slope, chrysanthemums by the road, and chrysanthemums in the center of the lawn. Although I didn't come to admire the chrysanthemums, I still have to glance at them a few times to appreciate whether the yellow ones are better or the white ones are better. At the same time, I ran to the wall of the large lawn while admiring the chrysanthemums to find a chair to sit and bask in the sun.

There are many Jiangbei mothers there taking care of foreign children playing. Some of them are knitting sweaters in their hands, leisurely. I finally found a chair and sat down, pretending to doze off while basking in the sun. Two mothers were chatting in a rustling voice, telling a love story. They thought I was asleep.

One of them, who was older, said, "He likes you." The other, who was younger, immediately replied with half embarrassment and half anger, "There is no such thing." The older one brought up the time and place to prove her words. She said, "Wasn't he talking to you very well by the back door yesterday?" The younger one was silent. I opened half an eye to glance at her. The blush on her face spread from her cheeks to the roots of her ears. I wanted to hear more, but the foreign children they were taking care of ran away while playing. They shouted loudly, "Oscar, Mary!" The conversation also stopped.

A French child rode a tricycle to my side and stopped, bumping my foot. He laughed loudly. I opened my eyes and looked at him. The child stared at me for a long time. I called out to exercise. He misunderstood what I meant, and for some reason, he started doing somersaults on the grass. His mother shouted at him from afar and ran over to pull his little hand away.

A group of Russian children surrounded me. I had met them a few days ago. They wanted me to get up and lead them in learning soldier gymnastics. The children are really naughty. I refused, so they all climbed on me and touched my beard. Moreover, some of them were behind me, pulling down the chair I was sitting on, causing me to fall down. There is really no way to deal with children! So, I stood up and gave orders according to their wishes.

The older ones in front and the younger ones in the back, they had already lined up, but one of the younger ones insisted on standing in front, and the older one refused. They argued and made a mess, rolling on the ground. It was hard to get them into formation, and when I told them to start walking, they ran away after only a few steps. If you run away, I can sit back in the chair and bask in the sun. I don't care, so I sat in the chair and closed my eyes.

However, they didn't just run away, but gathered together again, and seeing that I was ignoring them, they ran back to me again. This is really annoying. I suggested telling them a story, and they agreed. And very innocently and warmly, they stared at me with their little eyes, listening to a story about gods and monsters.

I thought of my younger siblings at home. My younger siblings at home often surrounded me and listened to me tell stories. However, after a life of wandering, I can't go home! After leaving the park, homesickness has been constant.

The Troubles of an Old Woman 225

— Wang

Cartoon on the Train 226

— Feng

The train rumbled along the tracks in the dark night. The third-class carriage was crowded with all kinds of people, making noise in various dialects, which made people panic. However, after the train had been running for an hour, under the attack of fatigue, the scene of unrestrained lying down, regardless of men or women, was truly a spectacle.

A female student with short hair, a white cloth shirt, and a black skirt walked into the carriage with a quilt and a box. She put the quilt in the overhead rack, and then lay down with the box as a pillow. At first, she was bending her feet, but later she stretched her feet straight and put them on the leg of a strange man; she was sleeping soundly and loudly; and the man was also sleeping sweetly as if nothing had happened, sometimes even putting one foot on the woman's thigh. Such a pair of strange men and women sleeping with their feet crossed does not mean that they do not know propriety, justice, and shame, but in the environment of this third-class seat, in the face of unbearable fatigue, they naturally do it. From this, one is reminded that those tricks of prohibiting men and women from traveling and eating together are just materials for after-dinner conversations!

Because everyone was lying down, it was as if this third-class carriage was like a mass burial ground. The fat man sitting blankly was like a grave keeper. The fat man was from the north, with a fat face, squinting eyes, and a mustache, looking like the Panchen Lama who once set up an altar in Hangzhou to pray for rain. He was always smiling, looking at the prostrate masses, silently smoking his pipe. Until the train entered the platform, the fat man never slept. This was not because he didn't want to sleep, but because all the seats were occupied. Therefore, he had no choice but to sit. That spirit of courtesy fully represents the Chinese people.

Speaking of the spirit of the Chinese people, this is also a masterpiece. That was when the train passed F station, and a few more people were added to the third-class carriage. Among them was a middle-aged man dressed in a long gown and mandarin jacket, who looked very gentlemanly. When he saw this scene like a mass burial ground, he shook his head and sighed: "What does this look like!" However, after a while, this middle-aged gentleman seemed to forget what he had just said, and stuffed himself into the mass burial ground and snored loudly; what does this look like? However, this courage is really admirable!

A figure who looked like a wandering hustler, with greasy hair, actually managed to pick up a middle-aged woman when the people in the car were only busy sleeping and didn't pay attention to him. They were originally sitting in the middle, but later quietly moved to that corner. Although there were a few soldiers guarding the car in that corner, they were all sound asleep, allowing the two people who had just met to negotiate the procedures for their progress.

Although the toilets were marked for men and women, the people in this third-class carriage seemed to care whether it was men or women, as long as it was a toilet. Once, a man walked into the women's toilet and closed the door, and a woman was waiting outside. Waiting, waiting, and still not seeing the man finish his business and come out, so she walked into the men's toilet. There was also a farce in which an old man and a woman were fighting to enter the women's toilet, which was staged in this third-class carriage.

When the train pulled into Shanghai North Station, it was already dawn. This third-class carriage became as noisy as when the train had just started. The middle-aged gentleman who "what does this look like" walked off the train with sleepy eyes. The female student with the white cloth shirt and black skirt walked away as if nothing had happened to her sleeping with her feet crossed with a strange man. The fat northerner who looked like the Panchen Lama was still smiling with squinting eyes. The people who were fighting for the toilet also dispersed. Only the greasy-haired man took the picked-up middle-aged woman away together. Everything, everything in this third-class carriage is changing like a "grand hotel", because it is also a microcosm of society!

On "Climbing the Dragon Gate" 227

— Dan Ran

Those preparing to embark on the path of literature almost all hope to "climb the dragon gate." Indeed, "climbing the dragon gate" is a crucial step in gaining status. Without "climbing the dragon gate," one cannot hear others call you a "literary writer." To walk the path of literature, one naturally wants to achieve "fame," and to achieve "fame," one must naturally think of "climbing the dragon gate." There is no need to oppose this. However, here I want to give a "wake-up call."

Recently, at a friend's house, I happened to come across a clipping from the Nanjing Chao Bao supplement, where I saw an article discussing "Zhang Kebiao's Job Advertisement." "Zhang Kebiao's Job Advertisement" was published in the classified ads of the Shen Bao, which I had not seen before. To avoid copying someone else's article, I excerpt the main points: "For several years, I have made a living by writing, claiming to be a freelance professional, but in reality, I am a dignified beggar. Now, for the sake of living, I seek a job."

Zhang Kebiao originally contributed the secret "Techniques for Climbing the Dragon Gate in the Literary World" to the general public. His "techniques for climbing the dragon gate" are certainly not bad. However, he is now "seeking a job for the sake of living."

From this, we can derive two answers:

First, although "climbing the dragon gate" seems to have certain boundaries, it ultimately has no real territory. Has Zhang Kebiao already "climbed the dragon gate"? If we say he "has not," then we can understand the difficulty of "climbing the dragon gate." If the author of the secret "Techniques for Climbing the Dragon Gate in the Literary World" cannot achieve the goal of "climbing the dragon gate," then those who have just embarked on the path of literature should "retreat in the face of difficulty"!

Second, from the fact that many people are familiar with the three characters "Zhang Kebiao," we can naturally say: "Zhang Kebiao has climbed the dragon gate." However, even someone who has already "climbed the dragon gate" still needs to "seek a job for the sake of living." Then, the value of "climbing the dragon gate" is very questionable. If "climbing the dragon gate" cannot solve one's own livelihood and one still needs a job, then 'those who yearn for "climbing the dragon gate" must prepare "supplies" early,' and this sentence must be printed on the cover when the "Techniques for Climbing the Dragon Gate in the Literary World" is reprinted to prevent people from following in Zhang Kebiao's footsteps.

I heard that in foreign countries, a writer does not have to worry about livelihood. If a decent work is published, one can eat and drink endlessly for life. But that is, after all, a foreign country. God destined you to be born in eastern Asia, so what can you do?

Finally, I want to erect a road sign, borrowing Sun Xizhen's words from "Me and Literature" to write on it: "This path cannot provide a secure livelihood."

In addition, I must declare: This article of mine is originally a discussion of the matter at hand, and I believe it is 'an expression of deep emotion.' I have no intention of disrespecting Mr. Zhang. Please forgive me, Mr. Zhang.

Amateur Mailbox

Lending Money to Someone to Bet on Dog Racing? 228

Editor:

You are the guide on the path of the lost, capable of providing considerable solutions and clarity for those who encounter difficult problems. I admire you very much. I now also have a question that I venture to ask, hoping you will publish it in the next few days when you have time. I would be eternally grateful.

Three years ago, I was an apprentice in a shop. There was a clerk, Mr. A, who was very close to me, but he had a bad habit. He could be said to never miss a dog race. Therefore, he gradually borrowed more than one hundred yuan from me. His purpose was mostly for this place. Among these funds, besides my family's money, there was also money entrusted to me by others for delivery, which he borrowed. When he borrowed the money, he always said that he could settle it soon and used sweet talk or invited me to go to the movies, etc. How could a young person like me resist such coaxing?

But now, because of pressure from others and my own financial difficulties, I have repeatedly asked him to return the money, but he ignores it as if nothing happened. Alas, what method can I use to ask him for the money? It is truly extremely difficult. Please, sir, provide a solution! Respectfully wishing you

Peace, Song Long

Editor's Note: When lending money to someone, there is a prerequisite: what will the person do with the money? If they are using it for a legitimate purpose, then we should help them and lend it to them. But if they are using it for an improper purpose, then we should refuse, because if you lend them money to do bad things, you become an accomplice to evil. Like Mr. Song's friend, who borrowed money to bet on dog racing, dog racing is a form of gambling and a very bad habit. Then, you should not lend him money. However, Mr. Song, because of his sweet talk and the temptation of movies, etc., not only lent him his own money, but also allowed him to swindle away other people's money to lose. This is Mr. Song's first mistake.

Also, there are two types of loans: one is a moral loan. This type of loan requires a deep friendship between the two parties, and the question of whether it will be repaid in the future is not discussed. Furthermore, the borrower's usual credit is also very good, so there is no need to write a loan agreement. The second type is a secured loan. This type of loan must have adequate collateral in advance, and a written agreement must be made, stating the repayment date, as proof for the future. Mr. Song's loan certainly cannot be considered a moral loan, but Mr. Song did not ask his friend to write a loan agreement, which is a big mistake. Because there is no written agreement, and according to the letter, it seems that there was no third party involved, then he can deny everything without regard for conscience. At that time, he is not legally responsible.

The only way to remedy the situation now is to quickly have him write you a loan agreement, preferably with someone as a witness. With a loan agreement, you should immediately ask him for the money and not delay any further.

Finally, the editor wants to declare that the purpose of publishing this letter is not to find a way for Mr. Song to recover the money, but to advise readers on some opinions about lending money to others, hoping everyone will pay attention to this point.

Storytelling with Musical Accompaniment 231

Yao Xiao'an Pang Xueqing Pearl Tower

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "Receiving the Vomit"

The jade beauty's singing and dancing have not yet returned,

Lonely Qin Tower, cold emerald terrace,

The precious mirror has not been put away, still connected,

Listening to the drumbeats of the night watch urging,

Lazy and wandering,

Happy to see the courtesan returning drunk,

Wine-drunk and rosy cheeks,

Helplessly, the emerald sleeves fall on both sides,

Bao Jian supports her, powerless and charming,

Beautiful resentment, shy head lazily raised,

Aunt Bao happily calls out there is a guest,

The beauty is drunk and unable to accompany,

Sleeping on the bed, starry eyes hazy,

Qin Zhong is chasing her, enjoying the good night in the fragrant boudoir,

Immediately takes a towel to personally receive the vomit,

Calling for tea, the verses follow, offering a dew cup.

The golden rooster awakens the immortal dream,

May I ask, who is this gentleman?

Little Miss, I am Qin Zhong, selling oil,

Last spring I saw and admired your talent,

Accumulating flower silver for a good meeting,

Last night, I chanced to meet you returning drunk,

Offering tea, I presumptuously received it,

Quickly took the clothes to wipe them,

The beauty listens and says it is rare,

Your sincerity is indeed heavy,

There is fate, all sorts of thanks and talent,

Carefully inquires when we will meet again.

Yu Xiaoxia Yu Xiaoyun Jade Dragonfly

Xinsheng (1380) 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM

Opening Chapter Wu Tenth Round "Farewell Brother"

Feng Gongpeng, the captain of the guards,

All the colleagues hold a farewell banquet for the week,

Wu Er returned home to say goodbye to his brother and sister-in-law,

Wu Dalang urged with tears,

Brother, today I come to part with you,

I do not know when you will return to the door,

Wu Er listened and stamped his feet,

Inevitably the hero also shed tears,

Calling out to his elder brother, don't worry,

Angrily glaring at the delicate and shy sister-in-law,

Sister-in-law, little uncle has words to tell you,

Do not look down on my brother as frivolous,

If there is any trouble,

I will teach you that your life will be difficult to keep,

Jin Lian listened and replied,

Saying that Wu Song's words are unreasonable,

As a sister-in-law, I am not a reckless man,

A fierce and lively woman,

Who is bullying my dear brother,

You quickly tell the reason,

D郎旁側來解勸，說道兄弟呀你我揮和中饌週，

My foolish brother will treat you to three cups of wine today,

Take care of your body and relieve my sorrow,

Feelings and nature, tears flow,

The colleagues urge Captain Wu,

Lift up and say goodbye to brother and sister-in-law,

Before leaving, turning his head several times,

Reluctant to leave his brother.

National Studies 233

Bingmei Ms. Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Topic: Stone Drum Song

Zhang Sheng holds the stone drum inscriptions in his hand,

And urges me to try to compose a Stone Drum Song.

Du Fu and Li Bai are no more,

With my meager talent, how can I cope with the Stone Drums?

The Zhou dynasty declined, and the world was in turmoil,

King Xuan rose in anger and wielded the heavenly halberd.

He opened the Mingtang wide to receive courtly homage,

And the swords and jade pendants of the dukes clanged as they rubbed against each other.

He hunted in Qishan, displaying his heroic prowess,

And the beasts of the field for ten thousand li were all swept into the net.

He carved the merits and achievements to proclaim to all generations,

Chiseling stones to make drums, demolishing towering heights.

The attending officials were all masters of talent and art,

Carefully selected to compose and carve, leaving a record on the mountains and rivers.

Rain and sun drenched, wild fires blazed,

Ghosts and spirits guarded it, needing constant protection.

From where did you obtain the paper copy?

Every detail is complete, without any errors.

The words are stern, the meaning dense, difficult to understand,

The script is unlike either the clerical script or the tadpole script.

After many years, how can it avoid missing strokes?

A quick sword can cut through and create dragons and mythical beasts.

Phoenixes soared and phoenixes danced, many immortals descended,

Coral and jade trees intertwined their branches.

Golden ropes and iron chains locked the buttons tightly,

Ancient tripods leaped in the water, dragons soared like shuttles.

Vulgar scholars cannot enter with their poetry,

The two elegant collections are cramped and without free-flowing style.

Confucius traveled west but did not reach Qin,

Holding a parasol, neglecting the stars, leaving behind righteous daughters.

Alas, I love antiquity but was born too late,

Facing this, tears flowed in torrents.

I remember when I was first summoned by the Imperial Academy,

That year, the era name was changed to Yuanhe.

An old friend serving in the right garrison,

Measured and excavated the old inscriptions for me.

I washed my crown and bathed, reporting to the Director of the Imperial Academy,

Such treasures, how many still exist?

They can be easily transported in felt bags and reed mats,

Ten drums only require a few camels.

Presented in the Imperial Ancestral Temple, comparable to ancient tripods,

Their value is more than a hundred times greater.

If the sacred grace allows them to remain in the Imperial Academy,

The students can discuss and learn together.

Viewing the classics, Hongdu is still choked with sobs,

Sitting and watching the whole country come running.

Chip away at the moss, scrape away the dirt, revealing the angles,

Place them properly, level and not tilted.

Build deep eaves and wide roofs to cover them,

Through long ages, hoping to remain without error.

High officials in the central court are old and experienced,

How can they be grateful or timid and hesitant?

Shepherds strike fire, oxen sharpen their horns,

Who will again take the hand to rub and polish?

Day by day, month by month, they will wear away and become buried,

For six years, gazing west, I empty sing.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Movies of "Semi-Colonies" 235

— Su Ping

"China is a semi-colony," many people say. Leaving aside politics, diplomacy, economics, and military affairs, these major national issues, let's just talk about Chinese movies, which also concretely reflect the characteristics of a semi-colony.

In the past, movies made by foreign overlords were always accepted by China unconditionally. Recently, foreign films have also been subject to censorship, but the supernatural and sensual films that Chinese people cannot make can be imported and publicly screened by foreign overlords. Movies that insulted China are no longer shown in China, but "The Good Earth," "The Oil Lamp," and other films that have some suspicion of insulting China can find Chinese people to act in them in mainland China.

Regarding foreign films, Chinese people have almost no right to choose. Hollywood can take movies to China after they are made, regardless of whether Chinese audiences understand the dialogue in the play. In other countries, the import and screening of foreign films is not so simple. American films going to France must be re-shot with French dialogue or have French subtitles added. French films going to Germany must be re-shot with German dialogue or have German subtitles added. Even in Japan, foreign films must have Japanese subtitles added. RKO's films even have to have Japanese actors re-shoot copies with Japanese dialogue in Tokyo! Chinese audiences are probably geniuses of language, and must understand English films, French films, German films, and Russian films. If they don't understand, foreign film merchants don't care, you can still go to the movie theater to practice foreign languages.

We have domestic movies, and our film companies can make movies themselves, which is of course very glorious. However, making movies must adhere to a certain scope and not overstep one's bounds. For example, scenes that harm the face of foreign overlords should not be filmed, so as not to harm diplomatic relations, which is understandable (whether movies that insult China harm diplomatic relations need not be discussed here). Things where foreign countries bully China and foreign overlords act domineeringly should also not be filmed, but this is for what? It is inevitable that people will be puzzled. As for the same event, the other country desperately films it to scold us, but we cannot even film newsreels that record the truth of the facts, and even if we film them, we cannot publicly screen them, which is even more incomprehensible. Therefore, movies of the Volunteer Army cannot be filmed, movies of the Battle of Shanghai are not good to film, the September 18th Incident is not good to film, and historical films of China being invaded cannot be filmed. A movie with allegorical nature like "Evil Neighbor" is not allowed to be made in the concessions, and "Sacrifice for the Country" must also be banned. Even a movie like "Shanghai Twenty-Four Hours," a sketch of life, is still far from being publicly screened because it involves a little patrol in the concessions. Recently, the situation has become even more severe. Subtitles such as "September 18th," "January 28th," and "Northeast" are not good to use, and maps of the four northeastern provinces should not be on the screen. The Chinese film industry is really too pitiful.

Foreign capital has invaded all aspects of Chinese business, and only the cultural business sector—no, strictly speaking, only the book industry and the film industry are still under the control of Chinese capital. However, according to recent newspaper reports, a Sino-foreign joint venture film company will appear in Shanghai. Originally, in foreign countries, there are also foreign capital-operated film businesses. Several major Hollywood companies have photography studios in England, Germany, and France, but the situation is different. If China has a Sino-foreign joint venture film company, not only will several domestic film companies have to close down, but even China's film business, no, even China's culture, will be under the control of foreign capital. Fortunately, it is still just a rumor now, and maybe it will not become a reality. Let's wait and see.

Film Reviews

Review of "The Black Cat" 236

— Stone Ax

"The Black Cat" at the Grand Theater

Since "eerie and terrifying," "ghastly," plus "clever mechanisms" and other similar films have been welcomed by some people, it has created opportunities for two people, Boris Karloff and Bela Lugosi. The former's makeup art, in addition to being "pleasing to the eye," has not had a peerless master like Lon Chaney before, and Karloff has certainly not yet discovered a similar "follower." The latter is known as "Big Bad Bela" in Hollywood, and of course he must have his own special advantages in portraying villains.

But in this "Black Cat," although it has "both beauties" and "two difficulties," it gives us nothing more than some tragic screams and some murderous art, and there are no other benefits. Furthermore, one may doubt whether there are still the murderous rituals of religions as described in Haggard's novels in such a world.

In order to protect the reason for "killing people," the script had to come up with some sacrificial patterns, so that many horror scenes could be created. Originally, horror films could not get rid of these clichés, but the layout of this film is too unevolved. Because it tried hard to increase the power of strangeness and desolation, it made people unable to "get goosebumps" after watching it.

Regarding the plot as mentioned above, then it is nothing more than seeing what strange things these two weirdos are doing again. Karloff has his own old routine, and Bela does not see any special features. The movements when the two fight are so clumsy that they don't look like real fights. The scenery is very useful in some new-style architectural patterns and three-dimensionality. We can't imagine that we can learn about decoration in watching mystery films.

Originally, Hollywood's producers were "clearly divided." Warner is known for its social short plays and classics, MGM is known for its modern realistic films, Columbia is a master of musical dance films, and United Artists is known for its artistic and literary films. Among the others, Universal's "superficial" and "large but inappropriate" films are the most. It is said that this film sold very well, so I think of when swordsmen novels were popular, there were indeed people who went to "abandon their homes and seek the Tao" and "fly" out of the window and fall to their deaths.

Audience Opinions

My View on "Grievance of a Lady" 237

— Nick

This is a play adapted from a literary work, so it must be discussed from another perspective.

Generally, films adapted from non-literary works succeed in another style through the compilation of plots and the depiction of characters. The former includes novels by Xiao E, Alexandre Dumas père, and Alexandre Dumas fils. The latter includes novels by Dickens, and also a film such as "Little Women." The former is naturally easier to render dynamically into movies, while the latter, even if it is edited to the best degree, is only about watching the expressions and actions of the actors. If it can be performed with "generosity and agitation," or "gentle tenderness," to the point where people have a feeling of "laughing and crying," it can also be said to be a very good result.

If we go to see a play whose script is adapted from a certain book or story or novel that we have always known, then we have a preconceived notion and hope before we watch it. Then, this type of play, although it can be a sensation for a while, is that preconceived notions differ from person to person, and the degree of satisfaction of hope cannot be consistent, so in terms of appreciation, it is discounted.

In my opinion, this "Grievance of a Lady" is only some skills in character depiction. From Norma Shearer to Maureen O'Sullivan, it has great success in trying to figure out the actions and personality of the people at that time, and they are all quite hardworking.

There is a roughly similar style to "Little Women" here, but "Little Women" is full of a "harmonious and auspicious" tone, while here it is everywhere "solemn" and "desolate." However, audiences who "do not seek deep understanding" and seek amusement may not be satisfied with this film.

"Mrs. Mai" to be Released 238

— Fire

"Mrs. Mai," directed by Zhang Shichuan, starring Hu Die and the famous dance troupe Liang sisters, is an all-dialogue and song sound film. It features a wavy story and stimulating descriptions, as well as interesting Cantonese opera excerpts: including "The Amorous History of Xuan Palace" performed by Xie Xingnong and Chen Jintang, "Ice Mountain Fire Line" and "The Heavenly Maiden Delivers a Son" performed by Zeng Sanduo, Xie Xingnong, and Feng Xiaofei, and "Who Will the Imperial Daughter Marry," Hu Die's first appearance on screen with Gua Ge Yang. The entire film is full of a soft Southern flavor and overflows with a wonderful romantic atmosphere. The actor worth mentioning is the Cantonese young man Hu Yixing. He is a basic actor of the Mingxing Film Company. Although he has not yet become famous on the screen, his handsome and refreshing expression here clearly shows that his future is limitless. The Liang sisters, Saizhu and Saisan, this pair of charming Southern beauties, also appear in this film. Although it's their first time on camera, their performance is surprisingly successful. The film will be released soon at the Xinguang Grand Theater. (Que)

Tianyi currently has a total of four sound machines, two in Shanghai and two in Hong Kong. It can be said to be one of the best in the domestic film industry.

A scene from Mingxing's new all-sound and dialogue film "Mrs. Mai" - directed by Zhang Shichuan, starring Hu Die and the Liang sisters, is scheduled to be released at the Xinguang Theater starting on the 28th of this month.

Submission Guidelines for the Shen Bao Film Supplement 242

This supplement is a film publication that assists cultural promotion and artistic expression. It welcomes external submissions, and will generously reward those that are published.

Once the text is published and rewarded, the copyright belongs to the Shen Bao.

The text in this supplement is mainly in vernacular Chinese and must use modern punctuation.

Each submission must be stamped with a seal, otherwise it will be rejected.

Texts, photos, etc., will not be kept or returned unless previously stated and return postage is attached.

Submissions that are sent to multiple publications, plagiarized, or copied from instructions will not be rewarded if discovered.

If the submission is a translation, the original work should be attached. English should be used sparingly in the text.

Do not write on both sides of the paper, or write horizontally, and do not use a pencil.

The space in this supplement is limited, so the text should be as concise as possible, with each submission limited to about 500 words.

Film Novel

Flying Flower Village (1) 243

— Yin Shi

Produced by Yihua Company, directed by Zheng Yingshi, starring Gao Zhanfei, Hu Ping, etc.

The spring breeze brings a warm breath to the world, and the scenery of Flying Flower Village is particularly charming. In the east of the village, there are several low houses in the shadows of flowers and green water, which are the flower garden and home of Ah Hua (played by Gao Zhanfei), who works as a cook on the train. In addition to going to work on the train every day, the planting, picking, and selling of flowers at home are handled by his old father (played by Qin Tong), who lost a left leg, and his young daughter Xiao Hua (played by Chen Juanjuan), and Xiao Hua's mother (Hu Ping) who work together.

Ah Hua's personality is very stubborn. When the stationmaster (played by Wang Naidong) gives him a lot of money and asks him to help smuggle private goods, he firmly refuses. The stationmaster believes that his refusal to go along with him has become an obstacle to their secret work, so he develops the determination to dismiss Ah Hua on the pretext of an excuse.

The wages that Ah Hua earns each month are very limited and are not enough to support his family. Fortunately, they can sell some flowers every day to supplement their household expenses. However, recently, due to the impact of the urban recession, the sales of flowers have also been affected, and they cannot even sell a single flower in a day.

One morning, Xiao Hua's mother, as usual, carried a basket of fresh flowers just picked from the garden to the flower market to sell, but unfortunately, she did not sell the flowers again. She anxiously wandered near the Flying Flower Village station and happened to be seen by the stationmaster. When he saw her beautiful demeanor, he couldn't help but be moved. So, the next day, when Ah Hua was not at home, he went to her house, but because Ah Hua's father was at home, he did not dare to make any presumptuous moves, only winked at her, gave Xiao Hua a silver dollar, and left.

It was a terrifying night of wind, rain, thunderstorms, and lightning. Ah Hua's father's old illness suddenly worsened. From his short breaths and the upward blinking of his eyes, it was clear that he was about to leave this world. When Xiao Hua's mother saw this terrifying scene, she hurriedly braved the rain and ran to the station in the dark to ask the stationmaster to allow Ah Hua to return immediately, but Ah Hua had been transferred by the main station to another section to drive a military train, and would not be back for four or five days.

When Xiao Hua's mother received this news, tears streamed down her face like a broken string. The clever stationmaster saw that the opportunity had arrived: he also generously took out a stack of banknotes from his pocket and gave them to her: "This is a small matter, I'll lend you some money first." Xiao Hua's mother gratefully took the money and ran back like lightning. However, the old grandfather had not waited for her return and had closed his eyes and passed away!

A few days later, Ah Hua returned. When he stepped into the house and saw his father's memorial tablet, he wailed and cried so much that he almost fainted. When Xiao Niang told him that the funeral expenses were lent by the stationmaster, Ah Hua couldn't help but burst into anger: he blamed Xiao Hua's mother for not borrowing money from such a bad person.

Ah Hua's father's death naturally gave the stationmaster great convenience. When Ah Hua was not at home, the stationmaster secretly ran over, and each time he brought many things to give to her. Xiao Hua's mother's will was shaken by the stationmaster's material and dedicated double temptation. Finally, one morning, she was anesthetized by the stationmaster's sweet words and, while Xiao Hua was fast asleep, followed the stationmaster to Shanghai. When they arrived in Shanghai, they traveled around many lively places and bought many fashionable clothes.

In the evening, the stationmaster coaxed her to a hotel, got her drunk, and achieved his goal of trampling on women. (To be continued)
